# [cite_start]CHAPTER 6 [cite: 1]

# [cite_start]HEAT-RESISTANT ALLOYS [cite: 1]

### [cite_start]6.1 GENERAL [cite: 1]

[cite_start]Heat-resistant alloys are arbitrarily defined as iron alloys richer in alloy content than the 18 percent chromium, 8 percent nickel types, or as alloys with a base element other than iron and which are intended for elevated-temperature service. [cite: 1] [cite_start]These alloys have adequate oxidation resistance for service at elevated temperatures and are normally used without special surface protection. [cite: 2] [cite_start]So-called "refractory" alloys that require special surface protection for elevated-temperature service are not included in this chapter. [cite: 3]

[cite_start]This chapter contains strength properties and related characteristics of wrought heat-resistant alloy products used in aerospace vehicles. [cite: 4] [cite_start]The strength properties are those commonly used in structural design, such as tension, compression, bearing, and shear. [cite: 5] [cite_start]The effects of elevated temperature are presented. [cite: 6] [cite_start]Factors such as metallurgical considerations influencing the selection of metals are included in comments preceding the specific properties of each alloy or alloy group. [cite: 6] [cite_start]Data on creep, stress-rupture, and fatigue strength, as well as crack-growth characteristics, are presented in the applicable alloy section. [cite: 7]

[cite_start]There is no standardized numbering system for the alloys in this chapter. [cite: 8] [cite_start]For this reason, each alloy is identified by its most widely accepted trade designation. [cite: 9]

[cite_start]For convenience in presenting these alloys and their properties, the heat-resistant alloys have been divided into three groups, based on alloy composition. [cite: 10] [cite_start]These groups and the alloys for which specifications and properties are included are shown in Table 6.1. [cite: 11]

[cite_start]The heat treatments applied to the alloys in this chapter vary considerably from one alloy to another. [cite: 12] [cite_start]For uniformity of presentation, the heat-treating terms are defined as follows: [cite: 13]

[cite_start]**Stress-Relieving** — Heating to a suitable temperature, holding long enough to reduce residual stresses, and cooling in air or as prescribed. [cite: 13]

[cite_start]**Annealing** — Heating to a suitable temperature, holding, and cooling at a suitable rate for the purpose of obtaining minimum hardness or strength. [cite: 14]

[cite_start]**Solution-Treating** — Heating to a suitable temperature, holding long enough to allow one or more constituents to enter into solid solution, and cooling rapidly enough to hold the constituents in solution. [cite: 15]

[cite_start]**Aging, Precipitation-Hardening** — Heating to a suitable temperature and holding long enough to obtain hardening by the precipitation of a constituent from the solution-treated condition. [cite: 16]

[cite_start]The actual temperatures, holding times, and heating and cooling rates used in these treatments vary from alloy to alloy and are described in the applicable specifications. [cite: 17]

[cite_start]6-1 [cite: 18]

### [cite_start]6.1.1 MATERIAL PROPERTIES [cite: 20]

#### [cite_start]6.1.1.1 Mechanical Properties [cite: 20]

[cite_start]The mechanical properties of the heat-resistant alloys are affected by relatively minor variations in chemistry, processing, and heat treatment. [cite: 20] [cite_start]Consequently, the mechanical properties shown for the various alloys in this chapter are intended to apply only to the alloy, form (shape), size (thickness), and heat treatment indicated. [cite: 21] [cite_start]When statistical values are shown, these are intended to represent a fair cross section of all mill production within the indicated scope. [cite: 22]

[cite_start]**Strength Properties** — Room-temperature strength properties for alloys in this chapter are based primarily on minimum tensile property requirements of material specifications. [cite: 23] [cite_start]Values for nonspecification strength properties are derived. [cite: 24] [cite_start]The variation of properties with temperature and other data or interest are presented in figures or tables, as appropriate. [cite: 24]

[cite_start]The strength properties of the heat-resistant alloys generally decrease with increasing temperatures or increasing time at temperature. [cite: 25] [cite_start]There are exceptions to this statement, particularly in the case of age-hardening alloys; [cite: 26] [cite_start]these alloys may actually show an increase in strength with temperature or time, within a limited range, as a result of further aging. [cite: 27] [cite_start]In most cases, however, this increase in strength is temporary and, furthermore, cannot usually be taken advantage of in service. [cite: 28] [cite_start]For this reason, this increase in strength has been ignored in the preparation of elevated temperature curves as described in Chapter 9. [cite: 29]

[cite_start]At cryogenic temperatures, the strength properties of the heat-resistant alloys are generally higher than at room temperature, provided some ductility is retained at the low temperatures. [cite: 29] [cite_start]For additional information on mechanical properties at cryogenic temperatures, other references, such as the Cryogenic Materials Data Handbook (Reference 6.1.1.1), should be consulted. [cite: 30]

[cite_start]**Ductility** — Specified minimum ductility requirements are presented for these alloys in the room-temperature property tables. [cite: 31] [cite_start]The variation in ductility with temperature is somewhat erratic for the heat-resistant alloys. [cite: 32] [cite_start]Generally, ductility decreases with increasing temperature from room temperature up to about 1200 °F to 1400 °F, where it reaches a minimum value, then it increases with higher temperatures. [cite: 33] [cite_start]Prior creep exposure may also affect ductility adversely. [cite: 34] [cite_start]Below room temperature, ductility decreases with decreasing temperature for some of these alloys. [cite: 34]

[cite_start]**Stress-Strain Relationships** — The stress-strain relationships presented are typical curves prepared as described in Section 9.3.2. [cite: 35]

[cite_start]**Creep** — Data covering the temperatures and times of exposure and the creep deformations of interest are included as typical information in individual material sections. [cite: 35] [cite_start]These presentations may be in the form of creep stress-lifetime curves for various deformation criteria as specified in Chapter 9 or as creep nomographs. [cite: 36]

[cite_start]**Fatigue** — Fatigue S/N curves for unnotched and notched specimens at room temperature and elevated temperatures are shown in each alloy section. [cite: 37] [cite_start]Fatigue crack propagation data are also presented. [cite: 38]

#### [cite_start]6.1.1.2 Physical Properties [cite: 38]

[cite_start]Selected physical-property data are presented for these alloys. [cite: 38] [cite_start]Processing variables and heat treatment have only a slight effect on these values; [cite: 39] [cite_start]thus, the properties listed are applicable to all forms and heat treatments. [cite: 40]

[cite_start]6-3 [cite: 41]

### [cite_start]6.2 IRON-CHROMIUM-NICKEL-BASE ALLOYS [cite: 41]

#### [cite_start]6.2.0 GENERAL COMMENTS [cite: 41]

[cite_start]The alloys in this group, in terms of cost and in maximum service temperature, generally fall between the austenitic stainless steels and the nickel- and cobalt-base alloys. [cite: 41] [cite_start]They are used in airframes, principally, in the temperature range 1000 to 1200 °F in those applications in which the stainless steels are inadequate and service requirements do not justify the use of the more costly nickel or cobalt alloys. [cite: 42]

#### [cite_start]6.2.0.1 Metallurgical Considerations [cite: 43]

[cite_start]**Composition** — The complex-base alloys comprising this group range from those in which iron is considered the base element to those which border on the nickel-base alloys. [cite: 43] [cite_start]All of them contain sufficient alloying elements to place them in the "Superalloy" category, yet contain enough iron to reduce their cost considerably. [cite: 44] [cite_start]Chromium, in amounts ranging from 10 to 20 percent or higher, primarily increases oxidation resistance and contributes to strengthening of these alloys. [cite: 45] [cite_start]Nickel and cobalt strengthen and toughen these materials. [cite: 46] [cite_start]Molybdenum, tungsten, and columbium contribute to hardness and strength, particularly at elevated temperatures. [cite: 46] [cite_start]Titanium and aluminum are added to provide age-hardening. [cite: 47]

[cite_start]**Heat Treatment** — The complex-base alloys are heat treated with conventional equipment and fixtures such as would be used for austenitic stainless steels. [cite: 47] [cite_start]Since these alloys are susceptible to carburization during heat treatment, it is good practice to remove all grease, oil, cutting, lubricant, etc., from the surface before heating. [cite: 48] [cite_start]A low-sulfur and neutral or slightly oxidizing furnace atmosphere is recommended for heating. [cite: 49]

#### [cite_start]6.2.0.2 Manufacturing Considerations [cite: 50]

[cite_start]The iron-chromium-nickel-base alloys closely resemble the austenitic stainless steels insofar as forging, cold forming, machining, welding, and brazing are concerned. [cite: 50] [cite_start]Their higher strength may require the use of heavier forging or forming equipment, and machining is somewhat more difficult than for the stainless steels. [cite: 51] [cite_start]Pertinent comments are included under the individual alloys. [cite: 52]

### [cite_start]6.2.1 A-286 [cite: 52]

#### [cite_start]6.2.1.0 Comments and Properties [cite: 52]

[cite_start]A-286 is a precipitation-hardening iron-base alloy designed for parts requiring high strength up to 1300 °F and oxidation resistance up to 1500 °F. [cite: 52] [cite_start]It is used in jet engines and gas turbines for parts such as turbine buckets, bolts, and discs, and sheet metal assemblies. [cite: 53] [cite_start]A-286 is available in the usual mill forms. [cite: 54]

[cite_start]A-286 is somewhat harder to hot or cold work than the austenitic stainless steels. [cite: 54] [cite_start]Its forging range is 2150 to 1800 °F; when finishing below 1800 °F, light reductions (under 15 percent) must be avoided to prevent grain coarsening during subsequent heat treatment. [cite: 55]

[cite_start]A-286 is readily machined in the partially or fully aged condition but is soft and "gummy" in the solution-treated condition. [cite: 56] [cite_start]A-286 should be welded in the solution-treated condition. [cite: 57] [cite_start]Fusion welding is difficult for large section sizes and moderately difficult for small cross sections and sheet. [cite: 57] [cite_start]Cracking may be encountered in the welding of heavy sections or parts under high restraint. [cite: 58]

[cite_start]A dimensional contraction of 0.0008 inch per inch is experienced during aging. [cite: 59] [cite_start]Oxidation resistance of A-286 is equivalent to that of Type 310 stainless steel up to 1800 °F. [cite: 60]

[cite_start]Some material specifications for A-286 alloy are presented in Table 6.2.1.0(a). [cite: 61] [cite_start]Room-temperature mechanical and physical properties are shown in Table 6.2.1.0(b). [cite: 62] [cite_start]The effect of temperature on physical properties is shown in Figure 6.2.1.0. [cite: 63]

[cite_start]6-4 [cite: 63]

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.2.1.0. Effect of temperature on the physical properties of A-286. [ALLOY:A-286]

**Axes** :

- X : Temperature, °F
- Y1 : K, Thermal Conductivity, Btu/[(hr)(ft²)(°F)/ft]
- Y2 : α, Mean coefficient of thermal expansion, 10⁻⁶ in./in./°F
- Y3 : C, Specific heat, Btu/(lb)(°F)

**Points clés (Valeurs approximatives extraites)** :

- **α (Coefficient d'expansion)** : 8.0 à 70 °F; 9.5 à 800 °F; 10.5 à 1600 °F.
- **K (Conductivité thermique)** : 7.0 à 70 °F; 11.5 à 800 °F; 14.5 à 1200 °F.
- **C (Chaleur spécifique)** : 0.10 à 70 °F; 0.13 à 800 °F.

**Description Narrative** :
Le graphique montre l'évolution des propriétés physiques de l'alliage A-286 en fonction de la température. La conductivité thermique (K) augmente de manière quasi linéaire et significative avec la température. Le coefficient moyen d'expansion thermique (α) suit également une tendance à la hausse stable sur toute la plage de température de 0 à 1600 °F. La chaleur spécifique (C) présente une croissance modérée avant de se stabiliser vers les hautes températures. [cite_start]Ces tendances indiquent un comportement thermique prévisible pour l'alliage A-286. [cite: 65, 66]

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.2.1.1.1. Effect of temperature on the tensile yield strength (Fty) and tensile ultimate strength (Ftu) of A-286 alloy (1800 °F solution treatment temperature). [ALLOY:A-286]

**Axes** :

- X : Temperature, °F
- Y : Percentage of Room Temperature Strength (%)

**Notes du graphique** :

- Strength at temperature. [cite_start]Exposure up to 1/2 hr. [cite: 69]

**Points clés (Valeurs approximatives extraites)** :

- **Ftu (Résistance ultime)** : 140% à -400 °F; 100% à 70 °F; ~85% à 1000 °F; ~70% à 1200 °F.
- **Fty (Limite élastique)** : ~125% à -400 °F; 100% à 70 °F; ~85% à 800 °F; ~85% à 1200 °F.

**Description Narrative** :
Ce graphique illustre la variation de la résistance en traction (Ftu et Fty) de l'alliage A-286 en pourcentage de sa valeur à température ambiante. On observe une augmentation significative de la résistance aux températures cryogéniques (jusqu'à 140% pour Ftu à -400 °F). À mesure que la température augmente au-dessus de l'ambiante, les deux propriétés diminuent graduellement. [cite_start]Fty reste relativement stable entre 800 °F et 1200 °F autour de 85%, tandis que Ftu chute plus rapidement au-delà de 1000 °F. [cite: 69, 70]

[cite_start]6-7 [cite: 71]

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.2.1.1.3. Effect of temperature on the bearing ultimate strength (Fbru) and the bearing yield strength (Fbry) for A-286 alloy (1800 °F solution treatment temperature). [ALLOY:A-286]

**Axes** :

- X : Temperature, °F
- Y : Percentage of Room Temperature Strength (%)

**Points clés** :

- **Fbry** : 100% à 70 °F; ~90% à 600 °F; ~85% à 1000 °F.
- **Fbru** : 100% à 70 °F; ~85% à 600 °F; ~80% à 1000 °F; ~68% à 1200 °F.

**Description Narrative** :
Le comportement au matage (bearing) montre une diminution constante avec la température. La résistance ultime au matage (Fbru) décline plus rapidement que la limite élastique au matage (Fbry). [cite_start]Une chute plus marquée est visible pour Fbru au-delà de 1000 °F. [cite: 71, 72]

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.2.1.1.4(a). Effect of temperature on the tensile and compressive moduli (E and Ec) for A-286 alloy (1800 °F solution treatment temperature). [ALLOY:A-286]

**Axes** :

- X : Temperature, °F
- Y : Percent E & Ec at Room Temperature (%)

**Points clés** :

- 100% à 70 °F.
- ~90% à 600 °F.
- ~80% à 1100 °F.
- ~72% à 1200 °F.

**Description Narrative** :
[cite_start]Les modules d'élasticité en traction (E) et en compression (Ec) diminuent de façon linéaire et modérée jusqu'à environ 1000 °F, après quoi la rigidité du matériau décroît plus brusquement. [cite: 73, 74]

[cite_start]6-8 [cite: 75]

[cite_start]Le coefficient de Poisson de l'alliage A-286 augmente de manière linéaire avec la température, passant d'environ 0.305 à l'ambiante à près de 0.345 à 1500 °F, indiquant une légère augmentation de la compressibilité latérale relative à haute température. [cite: 77, 78]

## Page 15

### 6.2.2 N-155 [ALLOY:N-155]

MIL-HDBK-5J 31 January 2003

### 6.2.2.0 Comments and Properties [ALLOY:N-155]

L'alliage N-155, également connu sous le nom de Multimet, est conçu pour des applications impliquant des contraintes élevées jusqu'à $1500^{\circ}F$. Il possède de bonnes propriétés d'oxydation, une bonne ductilité et peut être fabriqué facilement par des méthodes conventionnelles.
Cet alliage a été utilisé dans de nombreuses applications aéronautiques, notamment les pièces de postcombustion, les chambres de combustion, les ensembles d'échappement, les pièces de turbine et les boulons.

Le N-155 est forgé facilement entre $1650^{\circ}F$ et $2200^{\circ}F$. Il est facilement formé par des méthodes conventionnelles ; des recuits intermédiaires peuvent être nécessaires pour restaurer sa ductilité. Cet alliage est usinable dans tous les états ; des vitesses de coupe lentes et un débit important de liquide de refroidissement sont requis.
La soudabilité du N-155 est comparable à celle des aciers inoxydables austénitiques.
La résistance à l'oxydation de la tôle N-155 est bonne jusqu'à $1500^{\circ}F$.

### Table 6.2.2.0(a). Material Specifications for N-155 Alloy [ALLOY:N-155]

| [ALLOY_ID] | Specification | Form            | Condition                                         |
| ---------- | ------------- | --------------- | ------------------------------------------------- |
| [N-155]    | AMS 5532      | Sheet           | [cite_start]Solution treated [cite: 217]          |
| [N-155]    | AMS 5585      | Tubing (welded) | [cite_start]Solution treated [cite: 217]          |
| [N-155]    | AMS 5768      | Bar and forging | [cite_start]Solution treated and aged [cite: 217] |
| [N-155]    | AMS 5769      | Bar and forging | [cite_start]Solution treated [cite: 217]          |

### 6.2.2.1 Solution-Treated Condition [ALLOY:N-155]

Des courbes à température élevée sont présentées dans les Figures 6.2.2.1.1(a) et (b), ainsi que 6.2.2.1.4(a) et (b). Les propriétés de rupture sous contrainte sont spécifiées à $1500^{\circ}F$ pour les tôles et à $1350^{\circ}F$ pour les barres et les pièces forgées.

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.2.2.0. Effect of temperature on the physical properties of N-155 alloy [ALLOY:N-155].

- **Axes** :
  - [cite_start]**Axe X** : Temperature, F (0 à 1600)[cite: 240].
  - [cite_start]**Axe Y (Gauche - K)** : Thermal Conductivity, Btu/[(hr)(ft²)(°F)/ft] (8 à 13)[cite: 223].
  - [cite_start]**Axe Y (Droite - α)** : Mean Coefficient of Thermal Expansion, $10^{-6}$ in./in./°F (8 à 10)[cite: 236].

  - [cite_start]Conductivité (K) à 400°F : ~8.4[cite: 234].
  - [cite_start]Conductivité (K) à 1100°F : ~11.6[cite: 234].
  - [cite_start]Expansion (α) à 400°F : ~8.5[cite: 229].
  - [cite_start]Expansion (α) à 1000°F : ~9.1[cite: 229].
  - [cite_start]Expansion (α) à 1600°F : ~10.0[cite: 229].
- **Description Narrative** : La conductivité thermique (K) augmente de manière linéaire avec la température. [cite_start]Le coefficient moyen d'expansion thermique (α) augmente également, mais suivant une courbe plus douce, montrant une expansion thermique croissante à mesure que le matériau chauffe[cite: 241].

  - [cite_start]**Axe X** : Temperature, F (0 à 2000)[cite: 263].
  - [cite_start]**Axe Y** : Per Cent $F_{tu}$ at Room Temperature (0 à 100)[cite: 251].

  - [cite_start]70°F : 100%[cite: 252].
  - [cite_start]600°F : ~85%[cite: 264].
  - [cite_start]1000°F : ~80%[cite: 264].
  - [cite_start]1200°F : ~75%[cite: 264].
  - [cite_start]1400°F : ~52%[cite: 264].
  - [cite_start]1600°F : ~32%[cite: 264].
  - [cite_start]2000°F : ~12%[cite: 264].
- [cite_start]**Description Narrative** : La résistance ultime ($F_{tu}$) diminue graduellement jusqu'à $1200^{\circ}F$, puis chute de manière drastique au-delà de cette température, ne conservant qu'environ 12% de sa résistance initiale à $2000^{\circ}F$[cite: 260, 264].

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.2.2.1.1(b). Effect of temperature on the tensile yield strength (Fty) of N-155 alloy [ALLOY:N-155].

  - [cite_start]400°F : ~80%[cite: 278].
  - [cite_start]800°F : ~68%[cite: 278].
  - [cite_start]1200°F : ~55%[cite: 278].
  - [cite_start]1600°F : ~38%[cite: 278].
  - [cite_start]2000°F : ~12%[cite: 278].
- **Description Narrative** : La limite d'élasticité ($F_{ty}$) montre une chute plus linéaire et régulière que la résistance ultime sur toute la plage de température. [cite_start]À $1200^{\circ}F$, l'alliage conserve environ 55% de sa limite d'élasticité ambiante[cite: 273, 278].

## Page 19

### 6.3 NICKEL-BASE ALLOYS [ALLOY:NICKEL-BASE]

MIL-HDBK-5J 31 January 2003

### 6.3.0 GENERAL COMMENTS [ALLOY:NICKEL-BASE]

Le nickel est l'élément de base de la plupart des alliages résistants à la chaleur pour les hautes températures. Bien qu'il soit plus cher que le fer, le nickel fournit une structure austénitique qui possède une plus grande ténacité et une meilleure aptitude au façonnage que les structures ferritiques de même niveau de résistance.

### 6.3.0.1 Metallurgical Considerations [ALLOY:NICKEL-BASE]

- [cite_start]**Composition** : Les éléments d'alliage communs pour le nickel sont le cobalt, le fer, le chrome, le molybdène, le titane et l'aluminium[cite: 321].
  - [cite_start]**Cobalt** : Améliore la résistance à haute température[cite: 322].
  - [cite_start]**Fer** : Renforce la matrice et réduit le coût[cite: 323].
  - [cite_start]**Chrome** : Augmente la résistance et la résistance à l'oxydation[cite: 324].
  - [cite_start]**Molybdène** : Contribue au durcissement par solution solide[cite: 324].
  - [cite_start]**Titane/Aluminium** : Permettent le durcissement par vieillissement via les précipités $Ni_{3}$(Ti, Al)[cite: 325].
- [cite_start]**Melting** : La fusion sous vide est conseillée pour les alliages durcissables par vieillissement[cite: 327].

- **Heat Treatment [ALLOY:NICKEL-BASE]** :
  - Les alliages de nickel sont sensibles à la fragilisation par le soufre. Il est essentiel d'éliminer graisse, huile et lubrifiants avant traitement.
  - Un contrôle rigoureux du four est nécessaire ; une surchauffe de seulement $35^{\circ}F$ peut altérer la résistance.
  - [cite_start]Après mise en solution, les alliages sont généralement trempés à l'eau (ou à l'air pour les sections lourdes [cite: 336]).
  - Pour le recuit de détente (stress-relief), il est vital de chauffer rapidement à travers la plage $1200^{\circ}F$ - $1400^{\circ}F$ (basse ductilité) pour éviter un vieillissement prématuré.

### 6.3.0.2 Manufacturing Considerations [ALLOY:NICKEL-BASE]

- [cite_start]**Forging** : Tous les alliages (sauf moulage) peuvent être forgés[cite: 342]. [cite_start]Les nuances durcissables par vieillissement nécessitent un équipement plus lourd[cite: 343].

6-19

## Page 20

### 6.3.0.2 Manufacturing Considerations (Continued) [ALLOY:NICKEL-BASE]

MIL-HDBK-5J 31 January 2003

- **Cold Forming [ALLOY:NICKEL-BASE]** : Presque tous les alliages corroyés en tôle sont formables à froid. [cite_start]Les alliages à haute résistance nécessitent des pressions plus élevées et des recuits plus fréquents[cite: 347].
- **Machining [ALLOY:NICKEL-BASE]** : Facilement usinables si les conditions optimales (outil, vitesse, avance) sont respectées.
- **Welding [ALLOY:NICKEL-BASE]** :
  - [cite_start]Alliages à renforcement de matrice : Pas de problèmes sérieux[cite: 350].
  - Alliages durcissables par vieillissement :
    1. [cite_start]Confiner le soudage au matériau recuit[cite: 353].
    2. [cite_start]Risque de fissuration élevé dans le matériau durci[cite: 354].
    3. [cite_start]Recuire les pièces sévèrement travaillées avant soudage[cite: 357].
    4. [cite_start]Chauffage rapide requis pour la détente après soudage[cite: 359].
    5. [cite_start]Les soudures par fusion peuvent n'afficher que 70 à 80 % de la résistance à la rupture du métal de base[cite: 360].
- **Brazing [ALLOY:NICKEL-BASE]** :
  - Réponse favorable pour les alliages au chrome (type inox austénitique).
  - Atmosphères : hydrogène sec, argon, hélium (point de rosée $\le -80^{\circ}F$) ou vide.
  - [cite_start]Les alliages Al-Ti sont difficiles à braser ; un nickelage ou ferrage préalable de 0.5 à 1 mil est souvent utilisé pour empêcher l'oxydation[cite: 367, 368].
  - Alliages de brasage types Ni-Cr-Si-B et Ni-Cr-Si (Nicrobraz) pour les hautes températures.

## Page 21

### 6.3.1 HASTELLOY X [ALLOY:Hastelloy X]

#### 6.3.1.0 Comments and Properties [ALLOY:Hastelloy X]

Hastelloy X is a nickel-base alloy used for combustor-liner parts, turbine-exhaust weldments, afterburner parts, and other parts requiring oxidation resistance and moderately high strength above $1450^{\circ}F$. [cite_start]It is not hardenable except by cold working and is used in the solution-treated (annealed) condition. [cite: 1, 2, 3]

[cite_start]Hastelloy X is available in all the usual mill forms. [cite: 4]

[cite_start]Hastelloy X is somewhat difficult to forge; forging should be started at $2150^{\circ}F$ to $2200^{\circ}F$ and continued as long as the material flows freely. [cite: 5] [cite_start]It should be in the annealed condition for optimum cold forming, and severely formed detail parts should be solution treated at $2150^{\circ}F$ for 7 to 10 minutes and cooled rapidly after forming. [cite: 6]

[cite_start]Machinability of Hastelloy X is similar to that of austenitic stainless steel; the alloy is tough and requires low cutting speeds and ample cutting fluids. [cite: 7, 8]

[cite_start]Hastelloy X can be resistance or fusion welded or brazed; large or complex fusion weldments require stress relief at $1600^{\circ}F$ for 1 hour. [cite: 9, 10]

Hastelloy X has good oxidation resistance up to $2100^{\circ}F$. [cite_start]It age hardens somewhat during long exposure between $1200^{\circ}F$ and $1800^{\circ}F$. [cite: 11]

[cite_start]Some material specifications for Hastelloy X are presented in Table 6.3.1.0(a). [cite: 12] [cite_start]Room-temperature mechanical and physical properties for Hastelloy X sheet are presented in Table 6.3.1.0(b). [cite: 13] [cite_start]AMS 5754 does not specify tensile properties for bars and forgings. [cite: 14] [cite_start]Figure 6.3.1.0 shows the effect of temperature on physical properties. [cite: 15]

#### Table 6.3.1.0(a). Material Specifications for Hastelloy X [ALLOY:Hastelloy X]

| [ALLOY_ID] + [CONDITION] | Specification | Form            | Condition                        |
| :----------------------- | :------------ | :-------------- | :------------------------------- |
| [Hastelloy X] [Annealed] | AMS 5536      | Sheet and plate | Solution heat treated (annealed) |
| [Hastelloy X] [Annealed] | AMS 5754      | Bar and forging | Solution heat treated (annealed) |

#### 6.3.1.1 Annealed Condition [ALLOY:Hastelloy X]

[cite_start]The effect of temperature on various mechanical properties is presented in Figures 6.3.1.1.1 and 6.3.1.1.4. [cite: 18] [cite_start]In addition, certain stress-rupture requirements at $1500^{\circ}F$ are specified in AMS 5536 and 5754 for Hastelloy X. Typical tensile stress-strain curves at room and elevated temperatures are presented in Figure 6.3.1.1.6(a). [cite: 19] [cite_start]Typical compressive stress-strain and tangent-modulus curves at room and elevated temperatures are presented in Figure 6.3.1.1.6(b). [cite: 20]

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.1.0. Effect of temperature on the physical properties of Hastelloy X. [ALLOY:Hastelloy X]

- **Axes :**
  - [cite_start]**Axe X :** Temperature, $^{\circ}F$ (de 0 à 1600). [cite: 43, 44]
  - [cite_start]**Axe Y (Gauche - K) :** Thermal Conductivity (K), $Btu/[(hr)(ft^{2})(^{\circ}F)/ft]$ (de 6 à 16). [cite: 27, 30]
  - [cite_start]**Axe Y (Milieu - C) :** Specific Heat (C), $Btu/(lb)(^{\circ}F)$ (de 0.10 à 0.20). [cite: 37, 38, 40]
  - [cite_start]**Axe Y (Droite - $\alpha$) :** Mean Coefficient of Thermal Expansion ($\alpha$), $10^{-6} in./in./^{\circ}F$ (de 6 à 10). [cite: 49, 50]
- **Coordonnées clés extraites :**
  - **K (Conductivité) :** (200, ~8.3), (600, ~10.5), (1000, ~12.5), (1400, ~14.5).
  - **C (Chaleur Spécifique) :** (200, ~0.115), (600, ~0.125), (1000, ~0.135), (1400, ~0.150).
  - **$\alpha$ (Expansion) :** (200, ~7.6), (600, ~8.0), (1000, ~8.5), (1600, ~9.2).
- **Description Narrative :** Le graphique illustre une corrélation positive entre la température et les trois propriétés physiques. La conductivité thermique (K) et la chaleur spécifique (C) augmentent de manière quasi linéaire avec la température. [cite_start]Le coefficient d'expansion thermique moyenne ($\alpha$), mesuré entre $70^{\circ}F$ et la température indiquée, montre une progression stable et ascendante à mesure que la température s'élève jusqu'à $1600^{\circ}F$. [cite: 45]

## Page 27

### 6.3.2 INCONEL 600 [ALLOY:Inconel 600]

#### 6.3.2.0 Comments and Properties [ALLOY:Inconel 600]

Inconel 600 is a corrosion-and heat-resistant nickel-base alloy used for low-stressed parts operating up to $2000^{\circ}F$. [cite_start]It is not hardenable except by cold working and is usually used in the annealed condition. [cite: 157]

[cite_start]Inconel 600 is available in all the usual mill forms. [cite: 158] It is readily forged between $1900^{\circ}F$ and $2250^{\circ}F$; [cite_start]"hot-cold" working between $1200^{\circ}F$ and $1600^{\circ}F$ is harmful and should be avoided; cold working below $1200^{\circ}F$ results in improved properties. [cite: 159, 160] [cite_start]The maximum annealing temperature is $1800^{\circ}F$ if minimum yield-strength requirements are to be met consistently. [cite: 161]

[cite_start]The alloy is somewhat difficult to machine; high-speed steel or cemented-carbide tools should be used. [cite: 163, 164] [cite_start]It can be resistance or fusion welded or brazed (using non-silver containing brazing alloy); large or complex fusion weldments should be stress relieved at $1600^{\circ}F$ for 1 hour. [cite: 165, 166]

[cite_start]Oxidation resistance is excellent up to $2000^{\circ}F$ in sulfur-free atmospheres, but the alloy is subject to attack in sulfur-containing atmospheres. [cite: 167, 168]

#### Table 6.3.2.0(a). Material Specifications for Inconel 600 [ALLOY:Inconel 600]

| [ALLOY_ID] + [CONDITION] | Specification | Form                    | Condition |
| :----------------------- | :------------ | :---------------------- | :-------- |
| [Inconel 600] [Annealed] | AMS 5540      | Plate, sheet, and strip | Annealed  |
| [Inconel 600] [Various]  | ASTM B166     | Bar and rod             | Various   |
| [Inconel 600] [Annealed] | AMS 5580      | Tubing, seamless        | Annealed  |
| [Inconel 600] [Annealed] | ASTM B564     | Forging                 | Annealed  |

[cite_start]6-27 [cite: 177]

## Page 31

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.2.0. Effect of temperature on the physical properties of Inconel 600 [ALLOY:Inconel 600]

**Axes :**

- [cite_start]**Axe X :** Temperature, °F (Plage de 0 à 1600 °F) [cite: 20]
- [cite_start]**Axe Y1 (Gauche externe) :** $K$, Thermal Conductivity, Btu/[(hr)(ft²)(°F)/ft] [cite: 4]
- [cite_start]**Axe Y2 (Gauche interne) :** $C$, Specific Heat, Btu/(lb)(°F) [cite: 8]
- [cite_start]**Axe Y3 (Droite) :** $\alpha$, Mean coefficient of thermal expansion, $10^{-6}$ in./in./°F [cite: 27]

**Points clés extraits :**

- **Courbe K (Conductivité thermique) :** 0 °F $\approx$ 8.2 ; 400 °F $\approx$ 9.8 ; 800 °F $\approx$ 11.5 ; 1200 °F $\approx$ 13.5 ; [cite_start]1600 °F $\approx$ 16.0 [cite: 1]
- **Courbe C (Chaleur spécifique) :** 0 °F $\approx$ 0.100 ; 400 °F $\approx$ 0.115 ; 800 °F $\approx$ 0.128 ; 1200 °F $\approx$ 0.140 ; [cite_start]1600 °F $\approx$ 0.150 [cite: 1]
- **Courbe $\alpha$ (Dilatation thermique) :** 200 °F $\approx$ 7.4 ; 600 °F $\approx$ 7.9 ; 1000 °F $\approx$ 8.4 ; 1400 °F $\approx$ 9.0 ; [cite_start]1600 °F $\approx$ 9.3 [cite: 1]

**Description Narrative :**
Le graphique illustre l'évolution de trois propriétés physiques de l'Inconel 600 en fonction de la température. La conductivité thermique ($K$) montre une augmentation linéaire et constante avec la chaleur. La chaleur spécifique ($C$) augmente également de façon régulière, bien que la pente s'adoucisse légèrement au-delà de 1000 °F. [cite_start]Le coefficient moyen d'expansion thermique ($\alpha$), calculé entre 70 °F et la température indiquée, progresse de manière quasi linéaire sur toute la plage de température, confirmant la stabilité dimensionnelle prévisible de l'alliage sous contrainte thermique. [cite: 1, 22]

**Légende du graphique :**

- [cite_start]$\alpha$ - Between 70 °F and indicated temperature [cite: 14]
- [cite_start]$K$ - At indicated temperature [cite: 15]
- [cite_start]$C$ - At indicated temperature [cite: 16]

## Page 32

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.2.1.1. Effect of temperature on the tensile ultimate strength ($F_{tu}$) and the tensile yield strength ($F_{ty}$) of Inconel 600 [ALLOY:Inconel 600]

**Axes :**

- [cite_start]**Axe X :** Temperature, °F [cite: 40]
- [cite_start]**Axe Y :** Percentage of Room Temperature Strength [cite: 28, 29]

**Points clés extraits :**

- **$F_{tu}$ (Tensile Ultimate) :** 400 °F $\approx$ 92% ; 800 °F $\approx$ 82% ; 1200 °F $\approx$ 65% ; [cite_start]1600 °F $\approx$ 20% [cite: 38]
- **$F_{ty}$ (Tensile Yield) :** 400 °F $\approx$ 90% ; 800 °F $\approx$ 78% ; 1200 °F $\approx$ 68% ; [cite_start]1600 °F $\approx$ 35% [cite: 37]

**Description Narrative :**
Ce graphique présente la dégradation des propriétés en traction de l'Inconel 600 après une exposition de 30 minutes à haute température. On observe une chute progressive et quasi parallèle de $F_{tu}$ et $F_{ty}$ jusqu'à 1000 °F. [cite_start]Au-delà de 1200 °F, la résistance ultime ($F_{tu}$) s'effondre beaucoup plus rapidement que la limite d'élasticité ($F_{ty}$), indiquant une perte majeure de la capacité de charge maximale du matériau à très haute température. [cite: 36, 41]

---

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.2.1.2. Effect of temperature on the compressive yield strength ($F_{cy}$) and the shear ultimate strength ($F_{su}$) of Inconel 600 [ALLOY:Inconel 600]

**Axes :**

- [cite_start]**Axe X :** Temperature, °F [cite: 54]
- [cite_start]**Axe Y :** Percentage of Room Temperature Strength [cite: 42, 43]

**Points clés extraits :**

- **$F_{su}$ (Shear Ultimate) :** 200 °F $\approx$ 98% ; 600 °F $\approx$ 95% ; 1000 °F $\approx$ 88% ; [cite_start]1200 °F $\approx$ 75% [cite: 52]
- **$F_{cy}$ (Compressive Yield) :** 200 °F $\approx$ 94% ; 400 °F $\approx$ 90% ; 800 °F $\approx$ 80% ; [cite_start]1000 °F $\approx$ 74% [cite: 51]

**Description Narrative :**
Le graphique montre la résistance en compression et en cisaillement. La résistance ultime au cisaillement ($F_{su}$) reste très stable jusqu'à 800 °F avant d'amorcer une descente. [cite_start]La limite d'élasticité en compression ($F_{cy}$) montre une sensibilité thermique plus marquée dès les basses températures, avec un palier relatif entre 300 °F et 600 °F, suivi d'une dégradation constante. [cite: 56]

**Notes techniques :**
Strength at temperature. [cite_start]Exposure up to 1/2 hr. [cite: 36, 50]

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.2.1.4. Effect of temperature on the tensile and compressive moduli ($E$ and $E_c$) of Inconel 600 [ALLOY:Inconel 600]

## Page 34

### 6.3.3 INCONEL 625 [ALLOY:Inconel 625]

#### 6.3.3.0 Comments and Properties [ALLOY:Inconel 625]

[cite_start]Inconel 625 is a solid-solution, matrix strengthened nickel-base alloy primarily for applications requiring good corrosion and oxidation resistance at temperatures up to approximately 1800 °F and also where such parts may require welding. [cite: 83] [cite_start]The strength of the alloy is derived from the strengthening effect of molybdenum and columbium; thus, precipitation hardening is not required and the alloy is used in the annealed condition. [cite: 84, 85] [cite_start]The strength is greatly affected by the amount of cold work prior to annealing and by the annealing temperature. [cite: 86] [cite_start]The material is usually annealed at 1700 to 1900 °F for time commensurate with thickness. [cite: 87] [cite_start]The properties in this section are restricted to that annealing range. [cite: 88] [cite_start]Because the alloy was developed to retain high strength at elevated temperatures, it resists deformation at hot working temperatures but can be readily fabricated with adequate equipment. [cite: 89] [cite_start]The combination of strength, corrosion resistance, and ability to be fabricated, including welding by common industrial practices, are the alloy's outstanding features. [cite: 90] [cite_start]Some material specifications for Inconel 625 are listed in Table 6.3.3.0(a). [cite: 91] [cite_start]Room-temperature mechanical and physical properties for Inconel 625 are listed in Tables 6.3.3.0(b) and (c). [cite: 92] [cite_start]Figure 6.3.3.0 shows the effect of temperature on the physical properties. [cite: 93]

#### Table 6.3.3.0(a). Material Specifications for Inconel 625 [ALLOY:Inconel 625]

| [ALLOY_ID] + [CONDITION_TEMPER] | Specification | Form                    | Condition |
| :------------------------------ | :------------ | :---------------------- | :-------- |
| [Inconel 625] [Annealed]        | AMS 5599      | Sheet, strip, and plate | Annealed  |
| [Inconel 625] [Annealed]        | AMS 5666      | Bar, forging, and ring  | Annealed  |

[cite_start][cite: 95]

#### 6.3.3.1 Annealed Condition [ALLOY:Inconel 625]

[cite_start]Elevated-temperature curves for tensile ultimate strength, tensile yield strength, tensile and compressive moduli, and Poisson's ratio are presented in Figures 6.3.3.1.1(a) and (b), as well as 6.3.3.1.4(a) and (b). [cite: 96] [cite_start]Typical stress-strain and tangent-modulus curves are shown in Figures 6.3.3.1.6(a) through (d). [cite: 97] [cite_start]Fatigue S/N curves are presented in Figures 6.3.3.1.8(a) through (d). [cite: 98]

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.3.0. Effect of temperature on the physical properties of Inconel 625 [ALLOY:Inconel 625]

**Axes :**

- [cite_start]**Axe X :** Temperature, °F [cite: 123]
- [cite_start]**Axe Y1 (Gauche externe) :** $K$, Btu/[(hr)(ft²)(°F)/ft] [cite: 99]
- [cite_start]**Axe Y2 (Gauche interne) :** $C$, Btu/(lb)(°F) [cite: 106]
- [cite_start]**Axe Y3 (Droite) :** $\alpha$, $10^{-6}$ in./in./°F [cite: 126]

**Points clés extraits :**

- **$K$ (Thermal Conductivity) :** 0 °F $\approx$ 5.8 ; 800 °F $\approx$ 9.8 ; [cite_start]1800 °F $\approx$ 14.8 [cite: 109]
- **$C$ (Specific Heat) :** 0 °F $\approx$ 0.095 ; 1000 °F $\approx$ 0.130 ; [cite_start]1800 °F $\approx$ 0.155 [cite: 121]
- **$\alpha$ (Expansion) :** 200 °F $\approx$ 7.1 ; 1000 °F $\approx$ 7.8 ; [cite_start]1800 °F $\approx$ 8.9 [cite: 126]

## Page 37

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.3.1.1(a). Effect of temperature on the tensile ultimate strength ($F_{tu}$) of annealed Inconel 625 sheet and bar. [ALLOY:Inconel 625]

**Axes :**

- [cite_start]**Axe X :** Temperature, °F [cite: 149]
- [cite_start]**Axe Y :** Percentage of Room Temperature $F_{tu}$ [cite: 140]

**Points clés extraits :**

- **$F_{tu}$ :** 200 °F $\approx$ 97% ; 600 °F $\approx$ 90% ; 1200 °F $\approx$ 80% ; 1400 °F $\approx$ 50% ; [cite_start]1600 °F $\approx$ 25% [cite: 150]

**Description Narrative :**
La résistance ultime en traction ($F_{tu}$) de l'Inconel 625 recuit montre une excellente rétention (80%) jusqu'à 1200 °F. [cite_start]Passé ce cap thermique, une chute extrêmement raide se produit, le matériau perdant la moitié de sa résistance entre 1200 °F et 1400 °F. [cite: 147, 150]

---

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.3.1.1(b). Effect of temperature on the tensile yield strength ($F_{ty}$) of annealed Inconel 625 sheet and bar. [ALLOY:Inconel 625]

**Axes :**

- [cite_start]**Axe X :** Temperature, °F [cite: 161]
- [cite_start]**Axe Y :** Percentage of Room Temperature $F_{ty}$ [cite: 152]

**Points clés extraits :**

- **$F_{ty}$ :** 200 °F $\approx$ 88% ; 600 °F $\approx$ 75% ; 1200 °F $\approx$ 68% ; [cite_start]1600 °F $\approx$ 42% [cite: 162]

**Description Narrative :**
Contrairement à $F_{tu}$, la limite d'élasticité ($F_{ty}$) diminue plus tôt (perte de 12% dès 200 °F) mais se stabilise sur un plateau relatif entre 600 °F et 1200 °F avant de chuter à nouveau. [cite_start]À 1600 °F, la limite d'élasticité est proportionnellement mieux conservée que la résistance ultime. [cite: 162]

**Notes techniques :**
Strength at temperature. [cite_start]Exposure up to 1/2 hr. [cite: 147, 157]

MIL-HDBK-5J
[cite_start]31 January 2003 [cite: 146]
[cite_start]6-37 [cite: 163]

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.3.1.4(a). Effect of temperature on the tensile and compressive moduli ($E$ and $E_c$) of annealed Inconel 625. [ALLOY:Inconel 625]

**Axes :**

- [cite_start]**Axe X :** Temperature, °F [cite: 177]
- [cite_start]**Axe Y :** Percentage of Room Temperature Modulus [cite: 165]

**Points clés extraits :**

- **Moduli (E & $E_c$) :** 200 °F $\approx$ 96% ; 600 °F $\approx$ 85% ; 1200 °F $\approx$ 80% ; [cite_start]1600 °F $\approx$ 50% [cite: 178]

**Description Narrative :**
Les modules élastiques montrent une réduction graduelle jusqu'à 1200 °F (80% de rétention). [cite_start]Au-delà de cette température, la rigidité du matériau s'effondre rapidement, perdant 30% de sa valeur restante en seulement 400 °F. [cite: 175, 178]

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.3.1.4(b). Effect of temperature on Poisson's ratio for annealed Inconel 625 bar. [ALLOY:Inconel 625]

**Axes :**

- [cite_start]**Axe X :** Temperature, °F [cite: 189]
- [cite_start]**Axe Y :** Poisson's Ratio at Temperature [cite: 179]

**Points clés extraits :**

- **Poisson's Ratio :** 70 °F $\approx$ 0.278 ; 800 °F $\approx$ 0.295 ; 1400 °F $\approx$ 0.340 (Pic) ; [cite_start]1600 °F $\approx$ 0.335 [cite: 190]

**Description Narrative :**
Le coefficient de Poisson augmente de manière quasi linéaire avec la température, passant d'environ 0.28 à l'ambiante à un maximum de 0.34 à 1400 °F. Une légère inflexion à la baisse est notée après 1400 °F. [cite_start]Les valeurs sont déterminées dynamiquement. [cite: 182, 184]

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.3.1.6(a). Typical tensile stress-strain curves for annealed Inconel 625 sheet at room and elevated temperatures. [ALLOY:Inconel 625]

[cite_start]Les paramètres de Ramberg-Osgood ($n$) varient de 23 (RT) à 12 (1600 °F). [cite: 204, 205, 216]

Le module tangent commence à 30 x $10^3$ ksi et chute à mesure que la contrainte dépasse 60 ksi, correspondant à l'entrée dans le domaine plastique. [cite_start]Paramètre de Ramberg-Osgood $n = 32$. ## Page 41

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.3.1.8(a). Best-fit S/N curves for annealed unnotched Inconel 625 bar, longitudinal direction [ALLOY:Inconel 625]

**Axes :**

- [cite_start]**Axe X :** Fatigue Life, Cycles (échelle logarithmique de $10^3$ à $10^8$). [cite: 26]
- [cite_start]**Axe Y :** Maximum Stress, ksi (de 60 à 130). [cite: 1, 10]

**Coordonnées clés (estimées par Stress Ratio R) :**

- **R = 0.50 (Cercles) :** ~127 ksi à $2 \times 10^5$ cycles ; ~112 ksi à $10^6$ cycles ; [cite_start]~110 ksi à $10^7$ cycles (Run-out). [cite: 23, 24]
- **R = 0.10 (Diamants) :** ~125 ksi à $5 \times 10^4$ cycles ; ~110 ksi à $1.5 \times 10^5$ cycles ; ~100 ksi à $2 \times 10^5$ cycles ; [cite_start]~70 ksi à $8 \times 10^6$ cycles. [cite: 22]
- **R = -0.50 (Croix +) :** ~115 ksi à $10^4$ cycles ; ~90 ksi à $10^5$ cycles ; ~75 ksi à $4 \times 10^5$ cycles ; [cite_start]~73 ksi à $5 \times 10^5$ cycles. [cite: 21]

**Description Narrative :**
Le graphique présente la durée de vie en fatigue pour des spécimens non entaillés ($K_t=1.0$) à température ambiante. On observe une diminution linéaire de la contrainte maximale admissible par rapport au logarithme du nombre de cycles. Les courbes sont décalées vers le haut pour des rapports de contrainte (R) plus élevés, indiquant que la contrainte moyenne positive augmente la contrainte maximale supportable pour une durée de vie donnée, bien que l'amplitude de contrainte diminue. [cite_start]La dispersion est modérée avec un coefficient $R^2$ de 90%. [cite: 18, 46]

### Correlative Information for Figure 6.3.3.1.8(a) [ALLOY:Inconel 625]

- **Properties:** TUS = 133.2 ksi; TYS = 73.8 ksi; Temp. [cite_start]= RT [cite: 32]
- [cite_start]**Specimen Details:** Unnotched, 0.250 inch diameter [cite: 33, 34]
- [cite_start]**Surface Condition:** Longitudinally polished [cite: 35]
- [cite_start]**Reference:** 6.3.3.1.8(a) [cite: 39]
- **Test Parameters:** Loading - Axial; Frequency - Unspecified; Temperature - RT; [cite_start]Environment - Air [cite: 38, 40, 41, 42]
- [cite_start]**No. of Heats/Lots:** 1 [cite: 43]
- [cite_start]**Equivalent Stress Equation:** $\text{Log } N_f = 24.49 - 9.62 \log(S_{eq})$ where $S_{eq} = S_{max}(1-R)^{0.42}$ [cite: 44]
- **Std. [cite_start]Error of Estimate, Log(Life):** 22.71 $(1/S_{eq})$ [cite: 45]
- [cite_start]**Standard Deviation, Log(Life):** 0.985 [cite: 46]
- [cite_start]**R²:** 90% [cite: 46]
- [cite_start]**Sample Size:** 27 [cite: 47]

[cite_start]**Note:** STRESSES ARE BASED ON NET SECTION [cite: 11, 12]
[cite_start]**Caution:** The equivalent stress model may provide unrealistic life predictions for stress ratios beyond those represented above. [cite: 48]

## Page 42

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.3.1.8(b). Best-fit S/N curves for annealed notched Inconel 625 bar, Kt=3.0 longitudinal direction [ALLOY:Inconel 625]

**Axes :**

- [cite_start]**Axe X :** Fatigue Life, Cycles (échelle logarithmique de $10^3$ à $10^8$). [cite: 74]
- [cite_start]**Axe Y :** Maximum Stress, ksi (de 40 à 130). [cite: 53, 60]

**Coordonnées clés (estimées par Stress Ratio R) :**

- **R = 0.50 (Cercles) :** ~120 ksi à $2 \times 10^4$ cycles ; ~100 ksi à $4 \times 10^4$ cycles ; ~70 ksi à $8 \times 10^5$ cycles ; [cite_start]~60 ksi à $10^7$ cycles (Run-out). [cite: 69, 70]
- **R = 0.10 (Diamants) :** ~100 ksi à $9 \times 10^3$ cycles ; ~80 ksi à $4 \times 10^4$ cycles ; ~65 ksi à $10^5$ cycles ; [cite_start]~55 ksi à $10^6$ cycles. [cite: 68]
- **R = -0.50 (Croix +) :** ~70 ksi à $1.5 \times 10^4$ cycles ; ~55 ksi à $10^5$ cycles ; ~50 ksi à $3 \times 10^5$ cycles ; [cite_start]~50 ksi à $10^6$ cycles. [cite: 67]

**Description Narrative :**
Ce graphique montre l'effet d'une entaille sévère ($K_t=3.0$) sur la résistance en fatigue. Comparé à la figure précédente (unnotched), les niveaux de contrainte maximale pour une même durée de vie sont significativement réduits (environ 40-50% de réduction). La pente des courbes reste négative et constante. La dispersion est faible ($R^2 = 92\%$). [cite_start]Les données montrent une convergence vers une limite de fatigue aux alentours de $10^7$ cycles. [cite: 66, 91]

### Correlative Information for Figure 6.3.3.1.8(b) [ALLOY:Inconel 625]

- **Properties:** TUS = 133.2 ksi; TYS = 73.8 ksi; Temp. [cite_start]= RT [cite: 79]
- **Specimen Details:** V-Groove, $K_t=3.0$; 0.375 inch gross diameter; 0.250 inch net diameter; 0.013 inch root radius; [cite_start]60° flank angle [cite: 80, 81, 82]
- [cite_start]**Surface Condition:** Polished [cite: 83]
- [cite_start]**Reference:** 6.3.3.1.8(a) [cite: 85]
- **Test Parameters:** Loading - Axial; Frequency - Unspecified; Temperature - RT; [cite_start]Atmosphere - Air [cite: 94, 95, 96, 97, 98]
- [cite_start]**No. of Heats/Lots:** 1 [cite: 86]
- [cite_start]**Equivalent Stress Equation:** $\text{Log } N_f = 19.08 - 7.70 \log(S_{eq})$ where $S_{eq} = S_{max}(1-R)^{0.45}$ [cite: 87, 88]
- **Std. [cite_start]Error of Estimate, Log(Life):** 14.31 $(1/S_{eq})$ [cite: 89, 90]
- [cite_start]**Standard Deviation, Log(Life):** 0.959 [cite: 91]
- [cite_start]**R²:** 92% [cite: 91]
- [cite_start]**Sample Size:** 26 [cite: 92]

[cite_start]**Note:** STRESSES ARE BASED ON NET SECTION [cite: 64, 65]

[cite_start]La tendance reste une décroissance logarithmique stable. [cite: 118, 132]

[cite_start]La corrélation est excellente ($R^2 = 96\%$), ce qui permet une prédiction très fiable pour cette configuration géométrique. [cite: 159, 179]

## Page 45

### 6.3.4 INCONEL 706 [ALLOY:Inconel 706]

#### 6.3.4.0 Comments and Properties [ALLOY:Inconel 706]

[cite_start]Inconel 706 is a vacuum-melted precipitation-hardened, nickel-base alloy with characteristics similar to Inconel 718 except that Inconel 706 has greatly improved machinability. [cite: 189] [cite_start]The alloy has good formability and weldability. [cite: 190] [cite_start]Like Inconel 718, Inconel 706 has excellent resistance to postweld strain-age cracking. [cite: 190]

[cite_start]Depending upon choice of heat treatment, this alloy may be used for applications requiring either (1) high resistance to creep and stress rupture up to 1300°F or (2) high-tensile strength at cryogenic temperatures or elevated temperatures for short times. [cite: 191] [cite_start]The creep-resistant heat treatment is characterized by an intermediate stabilizing treatment before precipitation hardening. [cite: 192] [cite_start]Inconel 706 also has good resistance to oxidation and corrosion over a broad range of temperatures and environments. [cite: 193]

[cite_start]Because of close relationship between heat treatment properties and application, the form and applications are listed with specifications in Table 6.3.4.0(a). [cite: 194] [cite_start]Room-temperature mechanical and physical properties are in Table 6.3.4.0(b). [cite: 195] [cite_start]The effect of temperature on physical properties is shown in Figure 6.3.4.0. [cite: 195]

### ### Table 6.3.4.0(a). Material Specifications for Inconel 706 [ALLOY:Inconel 706]

| [ALLOY_ID]    | Specification | Form                    | Application   | Condition/Treatment                                                                   |
| ------------- | ------------- | ----------------------- | ------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| [Inconel 706] | AMS 5605      | Sheet, strip, and plate | Tensile       | [cite_start]1800°F solution treated [cite: 197]                                       |
| [Inconel 706] | AMS 5606      | Sheet, strip, and plate | Creep-rupture | [cite_start]1750°F solution treated [cite: 197]                                       |
| [Inconel 706] | AMS 5701      | Bar, forging, and ring  | Tensile       | [cite_start]1800°F solution treated [cite: 197]                                       |
| [Inconel 706] | AMS 5702      | Bar, forging, and ring  | Creep-rupture | [cite_start]1750°F solution treated [cite: 197]                                       |
| [Inconel 706] | AMS 5703      | Bar, forging, and ring  | Creep-rupture | [cite_start]1750°F solution treated, stabilized and precipitation treated [cite: 197] |

#### 6.3.4.1 Solution-Treated and Aged Condition (Creep Rupture Heat Treatment) [ALLOY:Inconel 706]

[cite_start]Effect of temperature on mechanical properties is shown in Figures 6.3.4.1.1, 6.3.4.1.4, and 6.3.4.1.5. [cite: 198] [cite_start]Typical tensile stress-strain curves are shown in Figure 6.3.4.1.6(a) and typical compressive stress-strain and tangent-modulus curves in Figure 6.3.4.1.6(b). [cite: 199] [cite_start]A full-range tensile stress-strain curve is shown in Figure 6.3.4.1.6(c). [cite: 200] [cite_start]Stress-rupture properties are specified at 1200°F; the appropriate specification should be consulted for detailed requirements. [cite: 201]

## Page 47

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.4.0. Effect of temperature on the physical properties of solution-treated and aged Inconel 706 [ALLOY:Inconel 706]

**Axes :**

- [cite_start]**Axe X :** Temperature, °F (de -500 à 2000). [cite: 237]
- [cite_start]**Axe Y1 (Gauche) :** K, Thermal Conductivity [Btu/(hr)(ft²)(°F)/ft] (de 6 à 16) et C, Specific Heat [Btu/(lb)(°F)] (de 0.10 à 0.20). [cite: 208, 211]
- [cite_start]**Axe Y2 (Droite) :** $\alpha$, Mean Coefficient of Thermal Expansion ($10^{-6}$ in/in/°F) (de 4 à 10). [cite: 262]

**Coordonnées clés :**

- **$\alpha$ (Expansion) :** ~6.8 at 250°F; ~8.2 at 1000°F; [cite_start]~9.8 at 1500°F. [cite: 220]
- **K (Conductivity) :** ~7.0 at 100°F; ~10.5 at 800°F; [cite_start]~12.8 at 1400°F. [cite: 223]
- **C (Specific Heat) :** ~0.10 at 0°F; ~0.13 at 1000°F; [cite_start]~0.15 at 2000°F. [cite: 223]

**Description Narrative :**
Les trois propriétés physiques augmentent de manière quasi linéaire avec la température. La conductivité thermique (K) et la chaleur spécifique (C) montrent une progression constante jusqu'à 1500°F-2000°F. [cite_start]Le coefficient d'expansion thermique ($\alpha$) augmente plus rapidement au début avant de se stabiliser légèrement vers les hautes températures. [cite: 238]

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.4.1.1. Effect of temperature on the tensile ultimate strength (Ftu) and the tensile yield strength (Fty) of Inconel 706 [ALLOY:Inconel 706]

**Axes :**

- [cite_start]**Axe X :** Temperature, °F (de 0 à 1600). [cite: 258]
- [cite_start]**Axe Y :** Percentage of Room Temperature Strength (de 0 à 100). [cite: 240]

**Coordonnées clés :**

- **$F_{tu}$ :** 100% at RT; ~90% at 400°F; ~85% at 1000°F; ~78% at 1200°F; [cite_start]~15% at 1600°F. [cite: 253]
- **$F_{ty}$ :** 100% at RT; ~91% at 400°F; ~83% at 1000°F; ~81% at 1200°F; [cite_start]~11% at 1600°F. [cite: 252]

**Description Narrative :**
La résistance (traction et limite élastique) reste relativement stable (perte <20%) jusqu'à environ 1100°F. Au-delà de 1200°F, on observe une chute brutale de la résistance, tombant à moins de 20% de la valeur initiale à 1600°F. [cite_start]Cela définit la limite opérationnelle supérieure de l'alliage pour les charges structurelles. [cite: 259]

[cite_start]6-47 [cite: 260]
[cite_start]MIL-HDBK-5J 31 January 2003 [cite: 217]

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.4.1.4. Effect of temperature on the tensile and compressive moduli (E and Ec) of Inconel 706 [ALLOY:Inconel 706]

**Axes :**

- [cite_start]**Axe X :** Temperature, °F (de 0 à 1600). [cite: 284]
- [cite_start]**Axe Y :** Percentage of Room Temperature Modulus (de 0 à 100). [cite: 263]

**Coordonnées clés :**

- **$E$ & $E_c$ :** 100% at RT; ~95% at 200°F; ~90% at 450°F; ~80% at 850°F; [cite_start]~71% at 1200°F. [cite: 276]

**Description Narrative :**
Le module d'élasticité (traction et compression) décroît de manière strictement linéaire avec l'augmentation de la température. [cite_start]À 1200°F, le matériau a perdu environ 29% de sa rigidité initiale par rapport à la température ambiante. [cite: 285]

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.4.1.5. Effect of temperature on the elongation (e) of solution treated and aged Inconel 706 [ALLOY:Inconel 706]

**Axes :**

- [cite_start]**Axe X :** Temperature, °F (de 0 à 1600). [cite: 303]
- [cite_start]**Axe Y :** Percent Elongation (e) (de 10 à 35). [cite: 286]

**Coordonnées clés :**

- **e :** ~17% at RT to 400°F; ~18.5% at 850°F; ~17% (dip) at 1000°F; ~21% at 1200°F; [cite_start]~28% at 1400°F. [cite: 294, 301]

**Description Narrative :**
L'allongement reste stable entre RT et 800°F. [cite_start]On note une légère chute (ductility dip) aux alentours de 1000°F avant une remontée très rapide au-delà de 1100°F, atteignant près de 30% à 1400°F, ce qui correspond à l'entrée dans le domaine de ductilité accrue à haute température. [cite: 304]

[cite_start]6-48 [cite: 305]
[cite_start]MIL-HDBK-5J 31 January 2003 [cite: 275]

[cite_start]Les paramètres Ramberg-Osgood varient de n=11 à RT jusqu'à n=9.2 à 1200°F. [cite: 352, 376]

## Page 51

### 6.3.5 INCONEL 718 [ALLOY:INCONEL 718]

#### 6.3.5.0 Comments and Properties [ALLOY:INCONEL 718]

Inconel 718 is a vacuum-melted, precipitation-hardened nickel-base alloy. [cite_start]It can be welded easily and excels in its resistance to strain-age cracking. [cite: 4] It is also readily formable. [cite_start]Depending on choice of heat treatments, this alloy finds applications requiring either (1) high resistance to creep and stress rupture to 1300°F or (2) high strength at cryogenic temperatures. [cite: 5] It also has good oxidation resistance up to 1800°F. [cite_start]Inconel 718 is available in all wrought forms and investment castings. [cite: 6] [cite_start]Because of the close relationship between heat treatment, properties, and applications, both the product form and application are listed with the specifications in Table 6.3.5.0(a). [cite: 7] [cite_start]Room-temperature mechanical and physical properties are presented in Tables 6.3.5.0(b) through (d). [cite: 8] [cite_start]The effect of temperature on physical properties is presented in Figure 6.3.5.0. [cite: 9]

### Table 6.3.5.0(a). Material Specifications for Inconel 718 [ALLOY:INCONEL 718]

| [ALLOY_ID] + [CONDITION]                  | Specification  | Form                | Application   |
| :---------------------------------------- | :------------- | :------------------ | :------------ |
| [INCONEL 718] [Solution-Treated and Aged] | AMS 5589       | Tubing              | Creep-rupture |
| [INCONEL 718] [Solution-Treated and Aged] | AMS 5590       | Tubing              | Short-time    |
| [INCONEL 718] [Solution-Treated and Aged] | AMS 5596       | Sheet, strip, plate | Creep-rupture |
| [INCONEL 718] [Solution-Treated and Aged] | AMS 5597       | Sheet, strip, plate | Short-time    |
| [INCONEL 718] [Solution-Treated and Aged] | AMS 5662, 5663 | Bar, forging        | Creep-rupture |
| [INCONEL 718] [Solution-Treated and Aged] | AMS 5664       | Bar, forging        | Short-time    |
| [INCONEL 718] [Solution-Treated and Aged] | AMS 5383       | Investment castings | Short-time    |

### 6.3.5.1 Solution-Treated and Aged Condition [ALLOY:INCONEL 718]

[cite_start]Elevated-temperature curves are presented in Figures 6.3.5.1.1 and 6.3.5.1.4(a) through (c). [cite: 12, 13, 14] [cite_start]Typical tensile and compressive stress-strain curves as well as typical compressive tangent-modulus curves for sheet and castings are shown in Figures 6.3.5.1.6(a) through (c). [cite: 14] [cite_start]Figure 6.3.5.1.6(d) is a typical stress-strain curve (full range) for Inconel 718 investment casting. [cite: 15] [cite_start]Creep and stress-rupture curves for forging are shown in Figures 6.3.5.1.7(a) through (e). [cite: 16] [cite_start]Supplemental creep and stress-rupture information for forging is presented in Table 6.3.5.1.7. [cite: 17] [cite_start]Fatigue S/N curves are presented in Figures 6.3.5.1.8(a) through (g). [cite: 18] [cite_start]Fatigue-crack-propagation data for die forging and plate are presented in Figures 6.3.5.1.9(a) through (c). [cite: 19]

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.5.0. Effect of temperature on the physical properties of Inconel 718. [ALLOY:INCONEL 718]

**Axes :**

- **Axe X :** Temperature, °F (Plage de -400 à 1600).
- **Axe Y1 (Gauche externe) :** C, Specific Heat, Btu/(lb)(°F).
- **Axe Y2 (Gauche interne) :** K, Thermal Conductivity, Btu/[(hr)(ft²)(°F)/ft].
- **Axe Y3 (Droite) :** $\alpha$, Mean Coefficient of Thermal Expansion, $10^{-6}$ in./in./°F.

**Points clés extraits (Valeurs approximatives) :**

- **Conductivité Thermique (K) :** 0°F $\approx$ 6.5; 400°F $\approx$ 8.2; 800°F $\approx$ 10.0; 1200°F $\approx$ 12.2; 1600°F $\approx$ 13.8.
- **Chaleur Spécifique (C) :** -100°F $\approx$ 0.08; 400°F $\approx$ 0.11; 800°F $\approx$ 0.125; 1600°F $\approx$ 0.15.
- **Expansion Thermique ($\alpha$) :** -200°F $\approx$ 6.2; 200°F $\approx$ 7.2; 600°F $\approx$ 7.7; 1000°F $\approx$ 8.2; 1600°F $\approx$ 9.5.

**Description Narrative :**
Le graphique illustre l'évolution des propriétés thermophysiques de l'Inconel 718 sur une large plage de températures. La conductivité thermique (K) et la chaleur spécifique (C) augmentent de manière quasi linéaire avec la température. Le coefficient moyen d'expansion thermique ($\alpha$) montre également une tendance à la hausse constante, partant d'environ $6 \times 10^{-6}$ à des températures cryogéniques pour atteindre près de $10 \times 10^{-6}$ à 1600°F. La progression est régulière sans changement de phase ou rupture brutale visible.

## Page 55

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.5.1.1. Effect of temperature on the tensile ultimate strength ($F_{tu}$) and tensile yield strength ($F_{ty}$) of solution-treated and aged Inconel 718. [ALLOY:INCONEL 718]

**Axes :**

- **Axe X :** Temperature, °F (Plage de -400 à 2400).
- **Axe Y :** Percentage of Room Temperature Strength (Plage de 0 à 200%).

**Points clés extraits (Valeurs approximatives) :**

- **-400°F :** $\approx$ 122% de la résistance à température ambiante (RT).
- **70°F (RT) :** 100%.
- **800°F :** $\approx$ 92%.
- **1200°F :** $\approx$ 85%.
- **1400°F :** Chute brutale, $\approx$ 45-50% ($F_{tu}$ et $F_{ty}$ divergent légèrement ici).
- **1600°F :** $\approx$ 30%.

**Description Narrative :**
Le graphique montre que l'Inconel 718 conserve une part importante de sa résistance jusqu'à environ 1200°F (plus de 80% de la valeur RT). Au-delà de 1200°F, on observe une chute drastique et quasi verticale de la résistance, indiquant la limite d'utilisation structurelle à haute température pour des expositions de courte durée (0.5 hr). Aux températures cryogéniques (-400°F), l'alliage gagne environ 20% de résistance par rapport à l'état ambiant.

**Note :** Strength at temperature. [cite_start]Exposure up to 1/2 hr. [cite: 89]

6-55
MIL-HDBK-5J
31 January 2003

## Page 56

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.5.1.4(a). Effect of temperature on dynamic tensile modulus (E) of solution-treated and aged Inconel 718. [ALLOY:INCONEL 718]

**Axes :**

- **Axe X :** Temperature, °F (-400 à 2000).
- **Axe Y :** Percentage of Room Temperature E (0 à 120%).

**Points clés extraits :**

- -200°F : $\approx$ 105%.
- 70°F : 100%.
- 800°F : $\approx$ 90%.
- 1200°F : $\approx$ 82%.
- 2000°F : $\approx$ 48%.

**Description Narrative :** Le module de traction dynamique diminue de façon linéaire et modérée jusqu'à 1000°F, puis la pente s'accentue légèrement au-delà de 1200°F, montrant une perte de rigidité plus marquée à très haute température.

---

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.5.1.4(b). Effect of temperature on dynamic shear modulus (G) of solution-treated and aged Inconel 718. [ALLOY:INCONEL 718]

**Axes :**

- **Axe X :** Temperature, °F (-400 à 2000).
- **Axe Y :** Percentage of Room Temperature G (0 à 120%).

**Points clés extraits :**

- -200°F : $\approx$ 107%.
- 70°F : 100%.
- 1000°F : $\approx$ 88%.
- 2000°F : $\approx$ 45%.

**Description Narrative :** Le comportement du module de cisaillement (G) est très similaire au module E, avec une décroissance constante à mesure que la température augmente.

[cite_start]**Note commune :** The reduction in dynamic modulus due to elevated temperature may be significantly less than the reduction in static modulus. [cite: 107, 122]

## Page 57

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.5.1.4(c). Effect of temperature on Poisson's ratio for solution-treated and aged Inconel 718. [ALLOY:INCONEL 718]

**Axes :**

- **Axe X :** Temperature, °F (-400 à 2000).
- **Axe Y :** Poisson's Ratio (0.21 à 0.41).

**Points clés extraits :**

- -300°F : $\approx$ 0.255.
- 70°F : 0.29 (Valeur nominale).
- 200°F à 800°F : Palier de stabilité relative entre 0.28 et 0.29.
- 1200°F : $\approx$ 0.30.
- 2000°F : $\approx$ 0.40.

**Description Narrative :** Le coefficient de Poisson est relativement stable (autour de 0.29) pour les températures d'usage courant (jusqu'à 1000°F). Au-delà de 1200°F, il augmente rapidement pour s'approcher de 0.40 à 2000°F, traduisant une transition vers un comportement plus plastique/ductile du matériau à très haute température.

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.5.1.7(a). Average isothermal 0.10% creep curves for Inconel 718 forging [ALLOY:Inconel 718]

- [cite_start]**Axe X :** Time to % Strain, Hrs (Échelle logarithmique de $10^0$ à $10^5$) [cite: 26, 31, 32]
- [cite_start]**Axe Y :** Stress, ksi (Échelle linéaire de 20 à 180) [cite: 1, 2, 26]
- [cite_start]**Courbes représentées :** Isothermes pour 1000°F, 1100°F, 1200°F et 1300°F[cite: 18, 19, 21, 23, 25].
- **Points de données clés (Valeurs approximatives extraites) :**
  - 1000°F : ~145 ksi à 50 hrs ; [cite_start]~120 ksi à 5000 hrs [cite: 1, 33]
  - 1100°F : ~120 ksi à 10 hrs ; [cite_start]~95 ksi à 2000 hrs [cite: 1, 33]
  - 1200°F : ~110 ksi à 3 hrs ; [cite_start]~75 ksi à 1000 hrs [cite: 1, 33]
  - 1300°F : ~80 ksi à 3 hrs ; [cite_start]~40 ksi à 300 hrs [cite: 1, 33]
- **Tendance narrative :** Les courbes montrent une relation inversement proportionnelle entre la contrainte appliquée et le temps nécessaire pour atteindre 0,10 % de déformation par fluage. On observe une chute significative de la résistance au fluage à mesure que la température augmente de 1000°F à 1300°F. À 1300°F, la courbe s'aplatit plus rapidement vers des niveaux de contrainte bas (environ 40 ksi) après seulement quelques centaines d'heures.

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.5.1.7(e). Average isothermal stress rupture curves for Inconel 718 forging [ALLOY:Inconel 718]

- [cite_start]**Axe Y :** Stress, ksi (20 à 180) [cite: 221, 222, 232]
- [cite_start]**Courbes représentées :** 1000°F, 1100°F, 1200°F, 1300°F[cite: 238, 240, 242, 244, 246].
- **Points de données clés :**
  - 1000°F : ~160 ksi à 50 hrs ; [cite_start]~120 ksi à 20000 hrs [cite: 221, 254]
  - 1100°F : ~135 ksi à 40 hrs ; [cite_start]~90 ksi à 30000 hrs [cite: 221, 254]
  - 1200°F : ~110 ksi à 30 hrs ; [cite_start]~65 ksi à 10000 hrs [cite: 221, 254]
  - 1300°F : ~85 ksi à 20 hrs ; [cite_start]~35 ksi à 20000 hrs [cite: 221, 254]
- **Tendance narrative :** Ces courbes représentent la durée de vie ultime avant rupture. La base de données est nettement plus fournie que pour les déformations spécifiques (162 tests). La pente est régulière, confirmant que l'alliage 718 conserve une excellente tenue structurelle jusqu'à 1100°F, mais voit ses capacités de charge à long terme s'effondrer au-delà de 1200°F.

  - [cite_start]$\Delta K = 80 \text{ ksi-in.}^{1/2}$ : $da/dN \approx 3 \times 10^{-4} \text{ in./cycle}$ [cite: 157]

La relation est quasi linéaire sur une échelle log-log, typique de la loi de Paris. On note une accélération de la propagation aux valeurs élevées de $\Delta K$ à l'approche de la rupture. [cite_start]Les données regroupent 193 points provenant de 7 spécimens. [cite: 153, 154, 159]

## Page 77

### 6.3.6 INCONEL X-750 [ALLOY:Inconel X-750]

#### 6.3.6.0 Comments and Properties [ALLOY:Inconel X-750]

Inconel X-750 is a high-strength oxidation-resistant nickel-base alloy. [cite_start]It is used for parts requiring high strength up to $1000^{\circ}F$ or high creep strength up to $1500^{\circ}F$ and for low-stressed parts operating up to $1900^{\circ}F$[cite: 272]. [cite_start]It is hardenable by various combinations of solution treatment and aging, depending on its form and application[cite: 272].

[cite_start]Inconel X-750 is available in all the usual wrought mill forms[cite: 273]. Inconel X-750 can be readily forged between $1900^{\circ}F$ and $2225^{\circ}F$; [cite_start]"hot-cold" working between $1200^{\circ}F$ and $1600^{\circ}F$ is harmful and should be avoided[cite: 274, 275]. [cite_start]This alloy is readily formed but should be solution treated at $1925^{\circ}F$ for 7 to 10 minutes after severe forming operations[cite: 276].

[cite_start]It is somewhat more difficult to machine than austenitic stainless steels[cite: 277]. [cite_start]Rough machining is easier in the solution-treated condition; finish machining in the partly or fully aged condition[cite: 277, 278]. [cite_start]Fusion welding is difficult for large section sizes and moderately difficult for small cross sections and sheet[cite: 278]. [cite_start]It must be welded in the annealed or solution-treated condition; weldments should be stress relieved at $1650^{\circ}F$ for 2 hours before aging[cite: 279, 280]. [cite_start]Nickel brazing, followed by precipitation heat treatment of the brazed assembly, results in strength nearly equal to fully heat-treated material[cite: 281].

[cite_start]Oxidation resistance of Inconel X-750 is good to $1900^{\circ}F$ but the beneficial effects of aging are lost above $1500^{\circ}F$[cite: 282]. [cite_start]This alloy is subject to attack in sulfur-containing atmospheres[cite: 283].

[cite_start]A variety of heat treatments has been developed for Inconel X-750[cite: 284]. [cite_start]Each provides special properties and renders the material in the best metallurgical condition for the intended application[cite: 285]. [cite_start]Only two of these heat treatments, for applications requiring high strength up to $1100^{\circ}F$, are described below[cite: 286]:

- [cite_start]**Annealed and Aged for Sheet, Strip, and Plate:** Mill annealed plus $1300^{\circ}F$ for 20 hours, and A.C. per AMS 5542[cite: 287].
- [cite_start]**Equalized and Aged for Bar and Forging:** $1625^{\circ}F$ for 24 hours, and $1625^{\circ}F$ for 4 hours, A.C., plus $1300^{\circ}F$ for 20 hours, and A.C. per AMS 5667[cite: 288, 290].

[cite_start]Other heat treatments are available for maximum creep-rupture strength[cite: 289].

### Table 6.3.6.0(a). Material Specifications for Inconel X-750 [ALLOY:Inconel X-750]

| [ALLOY_ID]      | Specification                    | Form                                            | Condition                         |
| :-------------- | :------------------------------- | :---------------------------------------------- | :-------------------------------- |
| [Inconel X-750] | [cite_start]AMS 5542 [cite: 295] | [cite_start]Sheet, strip, and plate [cite: 295] | [cite_start]Annealed [cite: 295]  |
| [Inconel X-750] | [cite_start]AMS 5667 [cite: 295] | [cite_start]Bar and forging [cite: 295]         | [cite_start]Equalized [cite: 295] |

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.6.0. Effect of temperature on the physical properties of Inconel X-750 [ALLOY:Inconel X-750]

- [cite_start]**Axe X :** Temperature, F (0 à 1600) [cite: 326, 327]
- [cite_start]**Axe Y1 (K) :** Thermal Conductivity, Btu/[(hr)(ft²)(F)/ft] (6 à 16) [cite: 306, 307, 316]
- [cite_start]**Axe Y2 (C) :** Specific Heat, Btu/(lb)(F) (0.10 à 0.20) [cite: 317, 318]
- [cite_start]**Axe Y3 ($\alpha$) :** Mean Coeff. of Thermal Expansion, $10^{-6}$ in./in./F (6 à 10) [cite: 322, 323, 345]
- **Description Narrative :** La conductivité thermique (K) et la chaleur spécifique (C) augmentent de façon quasi linéaire avec la température. [cite_start]Le coefficient de dilatation thermique ($\alpha$) augmente également de manière stable entre 70°F et 1600°F. [cite: 328]

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.6.1.1. Effect of temperature on $F_{tu}$ and $F_{ty}$ of Inconel X-750 sheet and plate [ALLOY:Inconel X-750]

- [cite_start]**Axe X :** Temperature, F (-400 à 1600) [cite: 339, 341, 342]
- [cite_start]**Axe Y :** Percentage of Room Temperature Strength (0 à 140) [cite: 329, 330, 331]
- **Description Narrative :** La résistance augmente aux températures cryogéniques (jusqu'à ~125% de la valeur à RT pour $F_{tu}$ à -400°F). À haute température, on observe un palier de stabilité relative entre 600°F et 1000°F, suivi d'une chute brutale de la résistance au-delà de 1100°F. [cite_start]À 1500°F, $F_{tu}$ tombe à environ 40% de sa valeur à température ambiante. [cite: 343]

**Notes Techniques :**

- [cite_start]Strength at temperature, Exposure up to 1/2 hr[cite: 337].
- [cite_start]AMS 5542[cite: 343].

- [cite_start]**Axe Y :** Percentage of Room Temperature Strength (0 à 100) [cite: 361, 362, 363]
- **Description Narrative :** Les propriétés de matage (Bearing) suivent une tendance similaire aux autres propriétés mécaniques, avec une stabilité relative jusqu'à 800°F, suivie d'une dégradation prononcée des performances. [cite_start]La résistance ultime en matage ($F_{bru}$) chute plus sévèrement que la limite élastique en matage ($F_{bry}$) aux très hautes températures. [cite: 374]

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.6.2.1(a). Effect of temperature on the tensile ultimate strength ($F_{tu}$) of Inconel X-750 bar (AMS 5667) [ALLOY:Inconel X-750 bar (AMS 5667)]

- **Axes** : X = Temperature (°F) ; Y = Percent $F_{tu}$ at Room Temperature (%).
- **Conditions** : Strength at temperature, Exposure up to 1/2 hr.
- **Points clés (X, Y)** :
  - (70, 100)
  - (400, 92)
  - (800, 89)
  - (1000, 88)
  - (1200, 78)
  - (1400, 48)
  - (1500, 34)
- **Description Narrative** : La résistance ultime à la traction ($F_{tu}$) de l'Inconel X-750 diminue de manière linéaire et modérée entre la température ambiante et 1000°F, conservant environ 88% de sa capacité. Au-delà de 1100°F, on observe une chute brutale et rapide de la résistance, tombant à seulement 34% à 1500°F.

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.6.2.1(b). Effect of temperature on the tensile yield strength ($F_{ty}$) of Inconel X-750 bar (AMS 5667) [ALLOY:Inconel X-750 bar (AMS 5667)]

- **Axes** : X = Temperature (°F) ; Y = Percent $F_{ty}$ at Room Temperature (%).
- **Conditions** : Strength at temperature, Exposure up to 1/2 hr.
- **Points clés (X, Y)** :
  - (70, 100)
  - (400, 92)
  - (800, 88)
  - (1100, 86)
  - (1300, 72)
  - (1500, 46)
- **Description Narrative** : La limite d'élasticité ($F_{ty}$) suit une tendance similaire à la résistance ultime. La stabilité est maintenue jusqu'à environ 1100°F avec une rétention de 86%. Une dégradation significative des propriétés mécaniques s'amorce après ce seuil thermique.

  - (1600, 70)
  - (1800, 63)
- **Note Technique** : The reduction in dynamic modulus due to elevated temperature may be significantly less than the reduction in static modulus.

Contrairement à la résistance mécanique, il n'y a pas de chute brutale, mais un affaiblissement progressif de la rigidité jusqu'à 1800°F.

- **Description Narrative** : Le module de cisaillement (G) décline de façon régulière. À 1200°F, l'alliage conserve environ 74% de sa rigidité au cisaillement initiale à température ambiante.

## Page 83

### 6.3.7 RENÉ 41 [ALLOY:René 41]

#### 6.3.7.0 Comments and Properties [ALLOY:René 41]

[cite_start]René 41 is a vacuum-melted precipitation-hardening nickel-base alloy designed for highly stressed parts operating between 1200°F and 1800°F. [cite: 56] [cite_start]Its applications include afterburner parts, turbine castings, wheels, buckets, and high-temperature bolts and fasteners. [cite: 57] [cite_start]René 41 is available in the form of sheet, bars, and forgings. [cite: 58]

[cite_start]René 41 is forged between 1900°F and 2150°F; small reductions must be made when breaking up an as-cast structure; [cite: 59] cracking may be encountered in finishing below 1850°F. [cite_start]René 41 work hardens rapidly, and frequent anneals are required; [cite: 60] [cite_start]to anneal, heat rapidly to 1950°F for 30 minutes and quench. [cite: 61]

René 41 is difficult to machine. [cite_start]In the soft solution-annealed condition it is gummy; [cite: 62] [cite_start]therefore, it should be in the fully aged condition for optimum machinability, and tungsten carbide cutting tools should be used. [cite: 63]

[cite_start]René 41 can be welded satisfactorily in the solution-treated condition; [cite: 64] [cite_start]after welding, the parts should be solution treated for stress relief. [cite: 65]

[cite_start]René 41 should not be exposed to temperatures above 2050°F during latter stages of hot working or during subsequent operations, otherwise severe intergranular cracking may be encountered. [cite: 66]

[cite_start]The oxidation resistance of René 41 is good to 1800°F. [cite: 67] [cite_start]Lengthy exposure above the aging temperature (1400°F to 1650°F) results in loss of strength and room-temperature ductility. [cite: 68]

[cite_start]Some material specifications for René 41 are shown in Table 6.3.7.0(a). [cite: 69] [cite_start]Room temperature mechanical and physical properties are shown in Table 6.3.7.0(b). [cite: 70] [cite_start]The effect of temperature on physical properties is shown in Figure 6.3.7.0. [cite: 71]

### Table 6.3.7.0(a). Material Specifications for René 41 [ALLOY:René 41]

| [ALLOY_ID] + [CONDITION_TEMPER]       | Specification | Form                    | Condition                                |
| :------------------------------------ | :------------ | :---------------------- | :--------------------------------------- |
| [René 41] [Solution treated]          | AMS 5545      | Plate, sheet, and strip | Vacuum melted, solution treated          |
| [René 41] [Solution treated and aged] | AMS 5712      | Bar and forging         | Vacuum melted, solution treated and aged |
| [René 41] [Solution treated and aged] | AMS 5713      | Bar and forging         | Vacuum melted, solution treated and aged |

#### 6.3.7.1 Solution Treated at 1975°F and Aged at 1400°F Condition [ALLOY:René 41]

[cite_start]Tensile and stress-rupture requirements at elevated temperatures are specified for René 41. The appropriate specification should be consulted for detailed requirements. [cite: 74] [cite_start]Other elevated-temperature data for René 41 in this condition are presented in Figures 6.3.7.1.1 through 6.3.7.1.5. [cite: 75] [cite_start]A creep nomograph for René 41 alloy sheet is shown in Figure 6.3.7.1.7. [cite: 76]

| [René 41] [Aged 1400°F]         | ALL         | ALL                      | S     | $\omega$ (Density)  | 0.298 lb/in³   |

**Notes:**

- a Design allowables were based upon data from samples of material, supplied in solution treated condition, which were aged to demonstrate heat treat response by suppliers. [cite_start]Properties obtained by the user may be different if the material has been formed or otherwise cold worked. [cite: 81, 82]
- b S-basis. [cite_start]The rounded $T_{99}$ value is 178 ksi. [cite: 83]

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.7.0. Effect of temperature on the physical properties of René 41 [ALLOY:René 41]

- **Axes** :
  - X = Temperature (°F).
  - Y1 (Gauche) = K (Conductivité thermique) en Btu/[(hr)(ft²)(°F)/ft].
  - Y1' (Gauche interne) = C (Capacité thermique massique) en Btu/(lb)(°F).
  - Y2 (Droite) = $\alpha$ (Coefficient d'expansion thermique) en $10^{-6}$ in./in./°F.
- **Courbes** :
  - **$\alpha$** : Entre 70°F et la température indiquée.
  - **K** : À la température indiquée.
  - **C** : À la température indiquée.
- **Points clés (X, Y)** :
  - **K** : (400, 8.8) ; (1000, 11.5) ; (1600, 14.8).
  - **C** : (400, 0.104) ; (1000, 0.118) ; (1600, 0.138).
  - **$\alpha$** : (200, 7.2) ; (800, 8.1) ; (1600, 9.4).
- **Description Narrative** : Les trois propriétés physiques augmentent de manière quasi linéaire avec la température. La conductivité thermique (K) montre la pente la plus raide, indiquant une meilleure transmission de chaleur à haute température. L'expansion thermique ($\alpha$) reste relativement stable, ne variant que de 2.2 unités sur une plage de 1400°F.

  - (800, 87)
  - (1200, 84)
  - (1400, 78)
  - (1800, 16)
- **Description Narrative** : Les résistances en traction (ultime et limite d'élasticité) sont très stables jusqu'à 1300°F. Une chute de performance extrêmement rapide est observée au-delà de 1400°F, le matériau perdant plus de 60% de sa résistance entre 1400°F et 1800°F.

  - **$F_{cy}$** : (1000, 84) ; (1400, 72) ; (1600, 24).
- **Description Narrative** : La résistance au cisaillement ($F_{su}$) se maintient mieux que la limite d'élasticité en compression ($F_{cy}$) entre 1200°F et 1500°F. Les deux propriétés s'effondrent après 1450°F.
