### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.7.1.7. Typical creep properties of René 41 sheet [ALLOY:René 41]

- **Axes** : Nomogramme complexe. Gauche : Time (hours) ; Centre : Creep Strain (%) ; Droite : Stress (ksi) par courbes de température.
- **Températures incluses** : 1250°F, 1400°F, 1600°F, 1800°F, 1850°F.
- [cite_start]**Exemple d'utilisation** : Temp = 1600°F, Stress = 7.5 ksi, Time = 10 hours $\rightarrow$ Creep Strain = 0.080%. [cite: 271-274]
- **Description Narrative** : Ce nomogramme permet de corréler le temps d'exposition sous contrainte avec la déformation de fluage résultante. Plus la température est élevée, plus la contrainte admissible pour un temps donné chute drastiquement.

#### Correlative Information for Figure 6.3.7.1.7 [ALLOY:René 41]

**Equation for Creep Strain (percent):**
[cite_start]$$\epsilon = 6.223 \times 10^7 \exp(-50760/T) \sigma^{[0.3928\exp(-2554/T)]} t^{[4.1557\exp(-3934/T)]}$$ [cite: 263-267]

- [cite_start]Temperature (T) = Fahrenheit + 460 [cite: 268]
- **Note** : This equation should only be used in the same temperature ranges indicated in the nomograph. [cite_start]Creep strains computed outside these temperature ranges may yield unreasonable values. [cite: 277, 278]

## Page 90

### 6.3.8 WASPALOY [ALLOY:Waspaloy]

#### 6.3.8.0 Comments and Properties [ALLOY:Waspaloy]

[cite_start]Waspaloy is a vacuum-melted precipitation-hardened nickel-base alloy which is strengthened by the precipitation of titanium and aluminum compounds and the solid-solution strengthening effects of chromium, molybdenum, and cobalt. [cite: 282] [cite_start]The alloy is designed for highly stressed parts operating at temperatures up to 1550°F such as aircraft gas turbine blades and discs and rocket engine parts. [cite: 283] [cite_start]It is available in all the usual mill forms. [cite: 284]

The optimum range for forging is 1900°F to 2050°F. [cite_start]Avoid working the alloy below 1900°F due to danger of cracking and also decreasing the stress-rupture life. [cite: 285] [cite_start]Sufficient soaking time between heating is necessary to ensure complete recrystallization; [cite: 286] [cite_start]however, avoid excessive long-time soaking at the high forging temperature. [cite: 287] [cite_start]Furnace atmospheres should be either neutral or slightly oxidizing to prevent carburization and to minimize scaling. [cite: 288]

Waspaloy is relatively difficult to machine. [cite_start]Drilling, turning, etc., can best be accomplished in solution-treated and partially aged condition. [cite: 289] Generally, carbide tools are preferred, and positive feeds are required to avoid work hardening. [cite_start]For finish machining, grinding is preferable. [cite: 290]

[cite_start]Waspaloy is susceptible to hot cracking or "hot-shortness" above 2150°F; [cite: 291] [cite_start]therefore, extreme care should be exercised in the design of weldments so that restraint can be minimized. [cite: 292] [cite_start]Waspaloy should be welded in the annealed condition, with minimum heat input, and with rapid cooling by means of chill bars and gas backup. [cite: 293]

[cite_start]This alloy has good resistance to oxidation at temperatures up to 1750°F and to combustion products encountered in aircraft gas turbines. [cite: 294]

### Table 6.3.8.0(a). Material Specifications for Waspaloy [ALLOY:Waspaloy]

| [ALLOY_ID] | Specification | Form                    |
| :--------- | :------------ | :---------------------- |
| [Waspaloy] | AMS 5544      | Plate, sheet, and strip |
| [Waspaloy] | AMS 5704      | Forgings                |
| [Waspaloy] | AMS 5706      | Bar, forging, ring      |
| [Waspaloy] | AMS 5707      | Bar, forging, ring      |
| [Waspaloy] | AMS 5708      | Bar, forging, ring      |
| [Waspaloy] | AMS 5709      | Bar, forging, ring      |

#### 6.3.8.1 Aged Condition [ALLOY:Waspaloy]

[cite_start]Stress rupture requirements at elevated temperatures are specified in material specifications. [cite: 302] The appropriate specification should be consulted for detailed requirements. [cite_start]The effect of temperature on various mechanical properties is shown in Figures 6.3.8.1.1, 6.3.8.1.4, as well as 6.3.8.1.5(a) and (b). [cite: 303]

MIL-HDBK-5J

## Page 92

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.8.0. Effect of temperature on the physical properties of Waspaloy. [ALLOY:Waspaloy]

- **Axes** : X = Temperature (°F); Y1 (Left) = K, $Btu/[(hr)(ft^{2})(^{\circ}F)/ft]$; Y2 (Middle) = C, $Btu/(lb)(^{\circ}F)$; Y3 (Right) = $\alpha$, $10^{-6} in./in./^{\circ}F$.
- **Points clés (Tendance)** :
  - **$\alpha$ (CTE)**: ~7.2 at 200°F, augmentant de façon quasi-linéaire jusqu'à ~9.2 à 1600°F.
  - **K (Conductivity)**: ~7.5 at 100°F, augmentant de manière exponentielle vers ~14.2 à 1600°F.
  - **C (Specific Heat)**: ~0.124 at 100°F, augmentant progressivement jusqu'à ~0.138 à 1600°F.
- **Description Narrative** : Le graphique montre que les trois propriétés physiques (conductivité thermique K, chaleur spécifique C et coefficient d'expansion thermique $\alpha$) augmentent avec la température. La conductivité thermique présente la pente la plus raide, doublant presque sur la plage de température de 0 à 1600°F.

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.8.1.1. Effect of temperature on the tensile ultimate strength ($F_{tu}$) and the tensile yield strength ($F_{ty}$) of Waspaloy. [ALLOY:Waspaloy]

- **Axes** : X = Temperature (°F); Y = Percentage of Room Temperature Strength.
- **Points clés (Tendance)** :
  - À 200°F : $F_{tu}$ et $F_{ty}$ sont à ~98%.
  - À 1000°F : Les deux sont à ~82%.
  - À 1200°F : Début du décrochage, ~80%.
  - À 1500°F : $F_{tu}$ chute brutalement à ~50% tandis que $F_{ty}$ se maintient mieux à ~68%.
- **Description Narrative** : La résistance reste relativement stable (perte de moins de 20%) jusqu'à environ 1000°F. Au-delà de 1200°F, la résistance ultime ($F_{tu}$) décline très rapidement par rapport à la limite d'élasticité ($F_{ty}$).

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.8.1.4. Effect of temperature on the modulus of elasticity (E) of Waspaloy. [ALLOY:Waspaloy]

- **Axes** : X = Temperature (°F); Y = Percentage of Room Temperature E.
- **Points clés (Tendance)** : 200°F (~98%), 600°F (~94%), 1000°F (~88%), 1400°F (~82%), 1600°F (~76%).
- **Description Narrative** : Le module d'élasticité diminue de manière linéaire et constante avec l'augmentation de la température, perdant environ 25% de sa valeur ambiante à 1600°F.

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.8.1.5(a). Effect of temperature on elongation (e) of Waspaloy. [ALLOY:Waspaloy]

- **Axes** : X = Temperature (°F); Y = Percent Elongation (e).
- **Points clés (Tendance)** :
  - **Bar and forging** : Constant à ~25% jusqu'à 1400°F, puis légère augmentation vers 28% à 1500°F.
  - **Sheet** : Constant à ~25% jusqu'à 800°F, puis chute rapide vers ~14% à 1400°F.
- **Description Narrative** : L'élongation se comporte différemment selon la forme du produit. Les barres et pièces forgées conservent ou augmentent leur ductilité à haute température, tandis que les tôles (sheet) subissent une perte de ductilité significative après 900°F.

source: "MIL-HDBK-5J"
page_pdf: "96"
units: "Imperial (ksi, °F, in)"

---

## Page 96

### 6.3.9. HAYNES® 230® [ALLOY:HAYNES 230]

### 6.3.9.0. Comments and Properties [ALLOY:HAYNES 230]

[cite_start]HAYNES® 230® alloy provides excellent oxidation resistance up to 2100°F for prolonged exposures with superior long term stability, high temperature strength and good fabricability. [cite: 131] [cite_start]It is produced in the form of plate, sheet, strip, foil, billet, bar, wire welding products, pipe, tubing, remelt bar, and may be cast using traditional air-melt sand mold or vacuum-melt investment foundry techniques. [cite: 132] [cite_start]Products are used for gas turbine components in the aerospace industry, catalyst grid supports in the chemical process industry, and various other high-temperature applications. [cite: 133]

[cite_start]**Environmental Considerations** — HAYNES 230 alloy has excellent corrosion resistance to both air and combustion gas oxidizing environments. [cite: 134] [cite_start]It also exhibits excellent nitriding resistance and good resistance to carburization and hydrogen embrittlement. [cite: 135]

[cite_start]**Machining** — HAYNES 230 alloy has similar machining characteristics to other solid-solution-strengthened nickel-based alloys. [cite: 136] [cite_start]This group of materials is classified moderate to difficult to machine, however, they can be machined using conventional methods at satisfactory rates. [cite: 137] [cite_start]They work-harden rapidly, requiring slower speeds and feeds with heavier cuts than would be used for machining stainless steels. [cite: 138] [cite_start]See HAYNES publication H-3159 for more detailed information. [cite: 139]

[cite_start]**Joining** — HAYNES 230 alloy has excellent forming and welding characteristics similar to HASTELLOY® X alloy. [cite: 140] [cite_start]It is readily welded using GTAW (Gas Tungsten-Arc Welding), GMAW (Gas Metal-Arc Welding), SMAW (Shielded Metal-Arc Welding), and resistance techniques. [cite: 141] [cite_start]HAYNES 230-WTM alloy is the recommended filler metal. [cite: 142]

[cite_start]**Heat Treatment** — This alloy is normally final solution heat-treated between 2150°F and 2275°F. [cite: 143] [cite_start]Annealing during fabrication can be performed at slightly lower temperatures, but a final subsequent solution heat treatment followed by rapid cooling is needed to produce optimum properties and structure. [cite: 143]

### Table 6.3.9.0(a). Material Specifications for HAYNES 230 Alloy Wrought [ALLOY:HAYNES 230]

| [ALLOY_ID]   | Specification | Form                    |
| :----------- | :------------ | :---------------------- |
| [HAYNES 230] | AMS 5878      | Plate, sheet, and strip |
| [HAYNES 230] | AMS 5891      | Bar and forging         |

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.9.0(a). Effect of temperature on specific heat of HAYNES 230 alloy. [ALLOY:HAYNES 230]

- **Axes** : X = Temperature (°F); Y = Specific Heat ($Btu/lb \cdot °F$).
- **Points clés (Tendance)** : 200°F (0.100), 600°F (0.108), 1000°F (0.112), 1200°F (0.134), 1800°F (0.147).
- **Description Narrative** : On observe une discontinuité notable entre 1000°F et 1200°F, où la chaleur spécifique bondit d'environ 20%, suggérant une transition de phase ou une modification structurelle avant de reprendre une croissance régulière.

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.9.0(b). Effect of temperature on thermal conductivity of HAYNES 230 alloy. [ALLOY:HAYNES 230]

- **Axes** : X = Temperature (°F); Y = Thermal Conductivity ($Btu \cdot in./ft^{2} \cdot hr \cdot °F$).
- **Points clés (Tendance)** : 200°F (75), 1000°F (130), 1800°F (195).
- **Description Narrative** : La conductivité thermique augmente de manière parfaitement linéaire avec la température sur toute la plage de 0 à 1800°F.

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.9.0(c). Effect of temperature on mean coefficient of thermal expansion of HAYNES 230 alloy. [ALLOY:HAYNES 230]

- **Axes** : X = Temperature (°F); Y = Coeff. of Thermal Expansion ($ppm/°F$).
- **Points clés (Tendance)** : 200°F (7.1), 1000°F (7.9), 1800°F (8.9).
- **Description Narrative** : Le coefficient d'expansion thermique moyen augmente de façon régulière et quasi-linéaire entre 70°F et 1800°F.

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.9.1.1(a). Effect of temperature on tensile properties of Haynes 230 alloy plate. [ALLOY:HAYNES 230]

- **Axes** : X = Temperature (°F); Y = Percentage of Room Temperature Strength.
- **Points clés (Tendance)** :
  - **$F_{tu}$** : 400°F (~90%), 1000°F (~80%), 1400°F (~60%), 2000°F (~18%).
  - **$F_{ty}$** : 400°F (~80%), 800°F (~70%), 1200°F (~68%), 2000°F (~18%).
- **Description Narrative** : Les deux propriétés de résistance ($F_{tu}$ et $F_{ty}$) diminuent avec la température. La limite d'élasticité ($F_{ty}$) chute plus tôt (dès 200°F) mais se stabilise entre 800°F et 1200°F, tandis que la résistance ultime ($F_{tu}$) décline plus tardivement mais de façon plus constante jusqu'à 2000°F.

## Page 101

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.9.1.1(b). Effect of temperature on tensile properties of HAYNES 230 alloy bar ranging up to 1.3 inches in diameter [ALLOY:HAYNES 230]

- **Axe X** : Temperature, °F (0 to 2200)
- **Axe Y** : Percentage of Room Temperature Strength (%)
- **Courbes** : $F_{tu}$ (Ultimate Tensile Strength) et $F_{ty}$ (Tensile Yield Strength)
- **Points clés (Valeurs approximatives extraites du graphique)** :
  - 75°F : 100% (Référence)
  - 600°F : $F_{tu} \approx 82\%$, $F_{ty} \approx 83\%$
  - 1000°F : $F_{tu} \approx 82\%$, $F_{ty} \approx 69\%$
  - 1400°F : $F_{tu} \approx 68\%$, $F_{ty} \approx 71\%$
  - 1800°F : $F_{tu} \approx 28\%$, $F_{ty} \approx 32\%$
  - 2000°F : $F_{tu} \approx 15\%$, $F_{ty} \approx 18\%$
- **Description Narrative** : Les propriétés de traction de l'alliage HAYNES 230 diminuent progressivement avec la température. On observe une chute plus marquée du $F_{ty}$ entre 600°F et 1000°F, tandis que le $F_{tu}$ reste relativement stable sur cette plage avant de décroître rapidement après 1200°F. À 2000°F, le matériau ne conserve qu'environ 15 à 18 % de sa résistance initiale à température ambiante.

### NOTES TECHNIQUES [ALLOY:HAYNES 230]

> The strain rate to determine TYS was 0.005 in/in/min of gage length. The crosshead rate to determine UTS strength from beyond yield strength was 0.5 in/min of reduced section length.

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.9.1.4. Effect of temperature on modulus of Haynes 230 alloy plate [ALLOY:HAYNES 230]

- **Axe X** : Temperature, F (0 to 2000)
- **Axe Y** : Percentage of Room Temperature Modulus, $10^6$ ksi (%)
- **Courbe** : Modulus at temperature
- **Points clés (Valeurs approximatives extraites du graphique)** :
  - 75°F : 100%
  - 600°F : $\approx 96\%$
  - 1000°F : $\approx 90\%$
  - 1400°F : $\approx 80\%$
  - 1800°F : $\approx 62\%$
- **Description Narrative** : Le module d'élasticité (Young) diminue de manière quasi linéaire à partir de 400°F. La perte de rigidité s'accélère légèrement aux températures extrêmes, atteignant environ 62 % de la valeur initiale à 1800°F.

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.9.1.5. Effect of temperature on elongation of Haynes 230 alloy plate [ALLOY:HAYNES 230]

- **Axe X** : Temperature, F (0 to 2000)
- **Axe Y** : Elongation, %
- **Points clés (Valeurs approximatives extraites du graphique)** :
  - 75°F : $\approx 53\%$
  - 800°F : $\approx 54\%$
  - 1200°F : $\approx 60\%$
  - 1600°F : $\approx 67\%$
  - 1800°F : $\approx 72\%$ (en pointillés)
- **Description Narrative** : L'allongement de l'alliage Haynes 230 augmente avec la température. La ductilité reste stable jusqu'à environ 800°F, puis augmente de façon constante pour dépasser les 70 % à 1800°F, ce qui est caractéristique des alliages à base de nickel à haute température.

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.9.1.6(a). Effect of temperature on Ramberg-Osgood parameter (n in tension) of Haynes 230 alloy plate [ALLOY:HAYNES 230]

- **Axe X** : Temperature, F (0 to 1600)
- **Axe Y** : Ramberg-Osgood, n
- **Points clés (Valeurs approximatives extraites du graphique)** :
  - 75°F : $\approx 18$
  - 400°F : $\approx 16$
  - 800°F : $\approx 18$
  - 1200°F : $\approx 27$
  - 1500°F : $\approx 38$
- **Description Narrative** : Le paramètre n de Ramberg-Osgood, qui décrit l'écrouissage du matériau, suit une courbe parabolique. Il diminue légèrement jusqu'à un minimum vers 400°F avant d'augmenter significativement avec la température, indiquant un changement de comportement plastique au-delà de 800°F.

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Figure 6.3.9.1.6 (i). Full range tensile stress-strain curves for Haynes 230 plate at 1600°F, 1700°F, and 1800°F [ALLOY:HAYNES 230]

- **Axe X** : Strain, in./in. (0.0 to 0.8)
- **Axe Y** : Stress, ksi (0 to 50)
- **Points de rupture (X sur le graphique)** :
  - 1600°F : Peak Stress $\approx 44$ ksi, Fracture Strain $\approx 0.65$ in./in.
  - 1700°F : Peak Stress $\approx 32$ ksi, Fracture Strain $\approx 0.58$ in./in.
  - 1800°F : Peak Stress $\approx 24$ ksi, Fracture Strain $\approx 0.70$ in./in.
- **Description Narrative** : À ces températures extrêmes, le matériau subit une déformation plastique très importante sous des contraintes faibles. On observe un pic de contrainte initial suivi d'une longue phase de "softening" (adoucissement) avant la rupture.

MIL-HDBK-5J
31 January 2003
6-108

## Page 109

### 6.3.10 HAYNES® HR-120®\* [ALLOY:HAYNES HR-120]

#### 6.3.10.0 Comments and Properties [ALLOY:HAYNES HR-120]

[cite_start]HAYNES HR-120 alloy is a solid-solution strengthened Fe-Ni-Cr alloy with excellent high temperature strength, very good resistance to carburizing and sulfiding environments, and readily formed hot or cold. [cite: 288]

[cite_start]**Environmental Considerations** - HAYNES HR-120 alloy has very good sulfide and carburization resistance. [cite: 289] [cite_start]Oxidation resistance is comparable to other Fe-Ni-Cr materials such as alloys 330 and 800H, yet with a greater strength at temperatures up to 2000°F. [cite: 290]

[cite_start]**Machining** - This alloy is readily machinable using conventional practices similar to those for 300 series austenitic stainless steels. [cite: 291] Minor adjustments may be required to yield optimum results. [cite_start]See HAYNES publication H-3125B for more detailed information. [cite: 292]

[cite_start]**Joining** - Welding characteristics are similar to the HASTELLOY® alloys. [cite: 293] [cite_start]The alloy is readily welded using GTAW (Gas Tungsten-Arc Welding), GMAW (Gas Metal-Arc Welding), and SMAW (Shielded Metal-Arc Welding) techniques. [cite: 293] [cite_start]HAYNES® 556™ alloy is the recommended filler wire (AMS5831) for GTAW and GMAW processes. [cite: 294] [cite_start]MultimetⓇ alloy covered electrode (AMS 5795) is recommended for SMAW processes. [cite: 295] [cite_start]HASTELLOY® X alloy filler wire (AMS 5798) and covered electrode (AMS 5799) may also be used. [cite: 296]

[cite_start]**Heat Treatment** - This alloy is solution annealed between 2150°F and 2250°F and rapidly cooled. [cite: 297]

[cite_start]**Specifications and Properties** - Material specifications are shown in Table 6.3.10.0(a). [cite: 298]

### Table 6.3.10.0(a). Material Specifications for HAYNES HR-120 Alloy Wrought Products [ALLOY:HAYNES HR-120]

| ------------------------------- | ------------- | ---------------------- |

  - (2000, 8) [cite_start][cite: 71, 76]

La limite élastique ($F_{ty}$) chute plus rapidement initialement (jusqu'à 500 F) avant de se stabiliser sur un plateau relatif entre 1000 F et 1500 F. À l'inverse, la résistance ultime ($F_{tu}$) reste plus élevée jusqu'à 1000 F, puis s'effondre brutalement après 1200 F. Fait notable : les deux courbes se croisent vers 1350 F, où le matériau conserve environ 60% de ses propriétés. [cite_start]Au-delà de 1500 F, la chute est sévère pour les deux propriétés. [cite: 79]

À 2200 F, le matériau ne peut supporter qu'une fraction minime de sa résistance nominale (environ 1 ksi pour 100 heures). [cite_start]La pente des courbes reste cohérente, indiquant un mécanisme de rupture par fluage stable. [cite: 137]

### 6.3.10.1.7 Stress Rupture Equation Data [ALLOY:HAYNES HR-120]

**Makeup of Data Collection:**

- [cite_start]**Heat Treatment:** Annealed [cite: 140]
- [cite_start]**Number of Vendors:** 1 [cite: 141]
- [cite_start]**Number of Test Laboratories:** 1 [cite: 149]
- [cite_start]**Number of Tests:** 283 [cite: 150]

**Specimen Details:**

- [cite_start]**Type:** 0.375 inch thick - Flat [cite: 152]
- [cite_start]**Other Types:** > 0.375 inch thick - 0.25 inch rd reduced section [cite: 153, 154]
- **Adjusted Gage Length:** 2.6 inches for flat specimens; [cite_start]1.35 inches for rd. specimens [cite: 156]
- **Gage Thickness:** 0.125" for flat specimens for sheets with thickness of 0.125" or greater. [cite_start]Sheet thickness for specimens from sheet with thickness < 0.125". [cite: 157]

[cite_start]**Stress Rupture Equation:** [cite: 145]
[cite_start]$$Log\ t = c + b_{1}/T + b_{2}X/T + b_{3}X^{2}/T + b_{4}X^{3}/T$$ [cite: 146]

- [cite_start]$T = °R$ [cite: 147]
- [cite_start]$X = log_{10}(\text{stress, ksi})$ [cite: 148]

**Constants:**

- [cite_start]$c = -16.671$ [cite: 158]
- [cite_start]$b_{1} = 49,051$ [cite: 159]
- [cite_start]$b_{2} = -8,375.3$ [cite: 160]
- [cite_start]$b_{3} = -2,403.7$ [cite: 161]
- [cite_start]$b_{4} = 619.59$ [cite: 162]

**Analysis Details:**

- [cite_start]**Standard Deviation:** 0.598 [cite: 164]
- [cite_start]**Standard Error of Estimate:** 0.155 [cite: 165]
- [cite_start]**Ratio of Between to Within Heat Treatment Variance:** < 0.10 (at spec pt.) [cite: 166]
- [cite_start]**$R^{2}$:** 96.6% [cite: 166]

> [cite_start]**Caution:** The stress rupture model may provide unrealistic times to rupture for stresses beyond those represented above. [cite: 167]

[cite_start]MIL-HDBK-5J 31 January 2003 [cite: 143]

## Page 116

### 6.4 COBALT-BASE ALLOYS [ALLOY:COBALT-BASE ALLOYS]

#### 6.4.0 GENERAL COMMENTS [ALLOY:COBALT-BASE ALLOYS]

[cite_start]The use of cobalt in wrought heat-resistant alloys is usually limited to additions of cobalt to alloys of other bases. [cite: 171] [cite_start]Very few of the heat-resistant alloys can be considered as cobalt base, since cobalt is seldom the predominating element. [cite: 172] [cite_start]For airframe applications, some workability is usually required; the alloys considered in this section are limited to those available in wrought form. [cite: 173]

#### 6.4.0.1 Metallurgical Considerations [ALLOY:COBALT-BASE ALLOYS]

- [cite_start]**Composition:** The common alloying elements for cobalt are chromium, nickel, carbon, molybdenum, and tungsten. [cite: 175]
- [cite_start]**Chromium:** Added to increase strength and oxidation resistance at very high temperatures. [cite: 176]
- [cite_start]**Nickel:** Added to increase toughness. [cite: 176]
- [cite_start]**Carbon:** Added to increase the hardness and strength, especially when combined with chromium and carbide formers (molybdenum and tungsten). [cite: 177]
- [cite_start]**Molybdenum and Tungsten:** Contribute to solid-solution strengthening. [cite: 178]
- [cite_start]**Melting:** Vacuum melting is not required for these alloys. [cite: 179]
- [cite_start]**Heat Treatment:** Cobalt-base alloys are heat treated with conventional equipment such as those used with austenitic stainless steels. [cite: 180] [cite_start]Heat-treating practices are not as critical as in the case of nickel-based alloys. [cite: 181]

#### 6.4.0.2 Manufacturing Considerations [ALLOY:COBALT-BASE ALLOYS]

- [cite_start]**Forging:** Require heavy forging equipment due to high strength near forging temperatures. [cite: 183] [cite_start]Forgeability is good over a wide range. [cite: 184] [cite_start]Hot-cold working is not required nor recommended. [cite: 185]
- [cite_start]**Cold Forming:** Excellent ductility in solution-treated condition. [cite: 186] [cite_start]Due to work hardening, they require higher pressures and frequent anneals. [cite: 187]
- **Machining:** Tough and work harden rapidly. [cite_start]Require heavy-duty vibration-free tools, sharp cutting tools (HSS or carbide), and low speeds. [cite: 188]
- [cite_start]**Welding:** Comparable to austenitic stainless steels. [cite: 190] [cite_start]All common processes are usable; large weldments require stress relief. [cite: 191]
- [cite_start]**Brazing:** Same as stainless steels and nickel alloys. [cite: 192] [cite_start]Alloys with Al or Ti require dry inert gas, high vacuum, or thin (0.002 to 0.0010 inch) nickel plating. [cite: 193] [cite_start]Braze in annealed condition with low stresses to avoid embrittlement. [cite: 194]

#### 6.4.0.3 Special Precautions [ALLOY:COBALT-BASE ALLOYS]

[cite_start]If not exposed to neutron radiation, no special precautions. [cite: 195] [cite_start]However, neutron irradiation creates **cobalt 60**, a dangerous radioactive isotope with a half-life of about 5.2 years. [cite: 196] [cite_start]Personnel must be protected from radioactive material. [cite: 197]

[cite_start]MIL-HDBK-5J 31 January 2003 [cite: 170]
[cite_start]6-116 [cite: 198]

condition_temper: "[Annealed, Solution Treated]"
product_form: "[Sheet, Plate, Bar, Forging]"
thickness_range: "[NOT_SPECIFIED]"

## Page 117

### 6.4.1 L-605 [ALLOY:L-605]

#### 6.4.1.0 Comments and Properties [ALLOY:L-605]

[cite_start]L-605, also known as **Haynes Alloy 25**, is a corrosion and heat-resistant cobalt-base alloy used for moderately stressed parts operating between 1000 and 1900 °F. [cite: 202] [cite_start]Applications include gas turbine blades and rotors, combustion chambers, and afterburner parts. [cite: 203] [cite_start]L-605 is not hardenable except by cold working and is usually used in the annealed condition. [cite: 204] [cite_start]Available in all mill forms. [cite: 205]

- [cite_start]**Forging:** Moderately well between 1900 °F and 2250 °F. [cite: 206]
- **Formability:** Excellent at room temperature in annealed condition. [cite_start]Severe parts should be annealed at 2225 °F for 7 to 10 minutes. [cite: 206, 207]
- [cite_start]**Machining:** Difficult; requires sharp tools and low speeds due to work hardening. [cite: 207, 208]
- **Welding/Brazing:** Fusion/resistance weldable or brazable. [cite_start]Large weldments stress relieved at 1300 °F for 2 hours. [cite: 209, 210]
- [cite_start]**Oxidation Resistance:** Excellent up to 1900 °F. [cite: 211]

### Table 6.4.1.0(a). Material Specifications for L-605 [ALLOY:L-605]

| [ALLOY_ID] + [CONDITION_TEMPER] | Specification | Form            | Condition                   |
| :------------------------------ | :------------ | :-------------- | :-------------------------- |
| [L-605] [Solution Treated]      | AMS 5537      | Sheet           | Solution treated (annealed) |
| [L-605] [Solution Treated]      | AMS 5759      | Bar and forging | Solution treated (annealed) |

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Effect of temperature on the physical properties of L-605 [ALLOY:L-605]

**Figure 6.4.1.0**

- [cite_start]**Axe X (Température) :** Temperature, F (-400 à 1600 F) [cite: 248, 249, 250, 251]
- [cite_start]**Axe Y Gauche (Conductivité K) :** K, Btu/[(hr)(ft²)(°F)/ft] (6 à 16) [cite: 226, 228, 232, 236, 237, 238, 239, 240, 248]
- [cite_start]**Axe Y Droite (Expansion $\alpha$) :** $\alpha, 10^{-6}$ in./in./F (4 à 10) [cite: 237, 241, 242, 243, 244, 245, 246, 247, 251]

**Courbe K (Conductivité thermique à température indiquée) :**

- (200 F, 6.2)
- (800 F, 9.8)
- (1200 F, 12.2)
- (1600 F, 15.0)

**Courbe $\alpha$ (Coefficient de dilatation moyen entre 70 F et température indiquée) :**

- (-400 F, 4.6)
- (0 F, 6.6)
- (800 F, 7.8)
- (1600 F, 9.1)

- **Description Narrative :** Le graphique montre une augmentation constante de la conductivité thermique (K) et du coefficient de dilatation thermique ($\alpha$) avec la température. [cite_start]La conductivité thermique s'accélère au-delà de 800 F. La dilatation thermique montre une croissance régulière depuis les températures cryogéniques (-400 F) jusqu'à 1600 F. Les deux courbes se croisent à une valeur numérique d'environ 9.8 vers 800 F sur leurs échelles respectives. [cite: 252]

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Effect of temperature on the tensile ultimate strength (Ftu) and the tensile yield strength (Fty) of L-605 [ALLOY:L-605]

**Figure 6.4.1.1.1**

- [cite_start]**Axe X (Température) :** Temperature, F (0 à 1800 F) [cite: 265-275]
- [cite_start]**Axe Y (Propriété) :** Percentage of Room Temperature Strength (0 à 100) [cite: 254-260]
- [cite_start]**Condition :** Exposure up to 1/2 hr [cite: 263]
- **Points de données clés (X, Y) :**
  - $F_{tu}$ à 1000 F : ~72%
  - $F_{tu}$ à 1400 F : ~54%
  - $F_{ty}$ à 600 F : ~58%
  - $F_{ty}$ à 1400 F : ~50%
- **Description Narrative :** La résistance ultime ($F_{tu}$) décline de manière linéaire jusqu'à 1200 F puis chute plus rapidement. [cite_start]La limite d'élasticité ($F_{ty}$) chute brutalement jusqu'à 600 F (atteignant ~58%), puis se stabilise sur un plateau remarquable entre 600 F et 1500 F avant de chuter à nouveau. [cite: 276]

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Effect of temperature on the compressive yield strength (Fcy) and the shear ultimate strength (Fsu) of L-605 [ALLOY:L-605]

**Figure 6.4.1.1.2**

- [cite_start]**Axe X (Température) :** Temperature, F (0 à 1800 F) [cite: 287-297]
- [cite_start]**Axe Y (Propriété) :** Percentage of Room Temperature Strength (0 à 100) [cite: 277-279, 282, 283, 285, 286]
- [cite_start]**Condition :** Exposure up to 1/2 hr [cite: 281]
- **Points de données clés (X, Y) :**
  - $F_{su}$ à 1000 F : ~70%
  - $F_{su}$ à 1400 F : ~50%
  - $F_{cy}$ à 600 F : ~64%
  - $F_{cy}$ à 1400 F : ~56%
- **Description Narrative :** Le comportement en compression ($F_{cy}$) et en cisaillement ($F_{su}$) suit une tendance similaire aux propriétés en traction. $F_{cy}$ présente un plateau de stabilité entre 600 F et 1200 F. $F_{su}$ décline plus régulièrement. [cite_start]Les deux courbes convergent vers 1200 F à environ 58% de la résistance initiale. [cite: 298]

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Typical creep properties of L-605 sheet [ALLOY:L-605]

- [cite_start]**Figure :** 6.4.1.1.7 [cite: 98]
- **Composants :** Nomogramme reliant le Temps (h), la Déformation de fluage (%), la Contrainte (ksi) et la Température (°F).
- [cite_start]**Axe X (Gauche) :** Time, hours (1 à 100 h) [cite: 94]
- [cite_start]**Axe X (Droite) :** Stress, ksi (1 à 40 ksi) [cite: 105]
- [cite_start]**Axe Y (Central) :** Strain, per cent (0.005 à 1.0 %) [cite: 81]
- **Équation de fluage :**
  [cite_start]$$\epsilon=(3.516\times10^{8}exp(-\frac{56040}{T}))(\begin{matrix}0.2791exp(\frac{3943}{T})\\ t\end{matrix})(\begin{matrix}0.4172exp(\frac{413.4}{T})\\ t\end{matrix})^{a}$$ [cite: 111]
- [cite_start]**Information corrélative :** $T = \text{Fahrenheit} + 460$[cite: 112].
- [cite_start]**Exemple d'utilisation :** Pour Temp $T=1600$ °F, Stress $\sigma=8$ ksi, Time $t=10$ hours, la déformation de fluage $\epsilon=0.091$ %. [cite: 114, 115, 116, 117]
- **Notes :** This equation should only be used in the same temperature ranges indicated in the nomograph. [cite_start]Creep strains computed outside these temperature ranges may yield unreasonable values. [cite: 119, 120]

## Page 124

### 6.4.2 HS 188 [ALLOY:HS 188]

#### 6.4.2.0 Comments and Properties [ALLOY:HS 188]

[cite_start]HS 188 is a corrosion- and heat-resistant cobalt-base alloy used for moderately stressed parts up to 2100 °F. [cite: 125] [cite_start]The alloy exhibits outstanding oxidation resistance up to 2100 °F resulting from the addition of minute amounts of lanthanum to the alloy system. [cite: 126] [cite_start]The alloy exhibits excellent post-aged ductility after prolonged heating of 1000 hours at temperatures up to 1600 °F inclusive. [cite: 127] [cite_start]HS 188 is not hardenable except by cold working and is used in the solution-treated condition. [cite: 128] [cite_start]The alloy can be forged and welded. [cite: 129] [cite_start]Welding can be accomplished by both manual and automatic welding methods including electron beam, gas tungsten air, and resistance welding. [cite: 129] [cite_start]Like other cobalt base alloys, machining is difficult necessitating the use of sharp tools and low cutting speeds; high speed steel or carbide cutting tools are recommended. [cite: 130, 131] [cite_start]Gas turbine applications include transition ducts, combustion cans, spray bars, flame-holders, and liners. [cite: 131]

#### Table 6.4.2.0(a). Material Specifications for HS 188 [ALLOY:HS 188]

| [ALLOY_ID] + [CONDITION_TEMPER]        | Specification | Form            | Condition                   |
| -------------------------------------- | ------------- | --------------- | --------------------------- |
| [HS 188] [Solution treated (annealed)] | AMS 5608      | Sheet and plate | Solution treated (annealed) |
| [HS 188] [Solution treated (annealed)] | AMS 5772      | Bar and forging | Solution treated (annealed) |

[cite_start][cite: 134, 135]

#### 6.4.2.1 Solution-Treated Condition [ALLOY:HS 188]

[cite_start]Elevated-temperature properties are presented in Figures 6.4.2.1.1(a) and (b), 6.4.2.1.2, 6.4.2.1.4(a) through (c), and 6.4.2.1.5. [cite: 138] [cite_start]Typical tensile stress-strain curves at room temperature are presented in Figure 6.4.2.1.6(a). [cite: 139] [cite_start]Typical compressive stress-strain and tangent-modulus curves at room and elevated temperatures are presented in Figure 6.4.2.1.6(b). [cite: 140] [cite_start]Strain control fatigue data for bar are presented in Figures 6.4.2.1.8(a) through (d). [cite: 141]

[cite_start]MIL-HDBK-5J 31 January 2003 [cite: 124]
[cite_start]6-124 [cite: 142]

| [HS 188] [Solution Treated]     | e (LT)             | <0.020          | S       | 40 percent        |
| [HS 188] [Solution Treated]     | e (LT)             | 0.020-0.187     | S       | 45 percent        |
| [HS 188] [Solution Treated]     | E                  | All             | Typical | 33.6 x $10^3$ ksi |
| [HS 188] [Solution Treated]     | $E_c$              | All             | Typical | 33.6 x $10^3$ ksi |
| [HS 188] [Solution Treated]     | G                  | All             | Typical | 12.8 x $10^3$ ksi |
| [HS 188] [Solution Treated]     | $\mu$              | All             | Typical | 0.31              |

### ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Effect of temperature on the physical properties of HS 188 [ALLOY:HS 188]

- [cite_start]**Figure :** 6.4.2.0 [cite: 172]
- **Axes Y :**
  - [cite_start]K : Thermal Conductivity, Btu/[(hr)(ft²)(°F)/ft] (6 à 18) [cite: 147, 150]
  - [cite_start]C : Specific Heat, Btu/(lb)(°F) (0.05 à 0.15) [cite: 162, 163]
  - [cite_start]$\alpha$ : Mean Coefficient of Thermal Expansion, $10^{-6}$ in./in./°F (5 à 12) [cite: 191, 188]
- [cite_start]**Axe X :** Temperature, F (-400 à 2800 °F) [cite: 171]
- **Points de données clés :**
  - [cite_start]$\alpha$ (at 1000 °F) $\approx$ 8.5 x $10^{-6}$ in./in./°F [cite: 151, 165]
  - [cite_start]K (at 1000 °F) $\approx$ 11 Btu/[(hr)(ft²)(°F)/ft] [cite: 154, 166]
  - [cite_start]C (at 1000 °F) $\approx$ 0.12 Btu/(lb)(°F) [cite: 156, 167]
- **Description Narrative :** Les trois propriétés physiques (conductivité, chaleur spécifique et expansion thermique) augmentent de manière quasi linéaire avec la température. [cite_start]La conductivité thermique (K) présente la pente la plus marquée. [cite: 172]

### [cite_start]ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Typical compressive stress-strain and compressive tangent-modulus curves for HS 188 sheet at various temperatures [ALLOY:HS 188] [cite: 41]

  - [cite_start]**Axe X (Inférieur - Tangent Modulus)** : Compressive Tangent Modulus, $10^{3}$ ksi (Échelle de 0 à 35) [cite: 40, 39]
  - **Axe X (Supérieur - Strain)** : Strain, 0.001 in./in. (Échelle de 0 à 14) [cite_start][cite: 27, 31]
- [cite_start]**Paramètres Ramberg-Osgood**[cite: 18, 20]:
  - $n (RT) = 13$
  - $n (600 F) = 13$
  - $n (1000 F) = 15$
  - $n (1400 F) = 18$
- [cite_start]**Orientation** : Long Transverse [cite: 15]
- **Points de données clés (Stress-Strain - Approximation visuelle)** :
  - [cite_start]**RT (Room Temp)** : (Strain 2, Stress 60), (Strain 4, Stress 70), (Strain 6, Stress 75) [cite: 4, 14]
  - [cite_start]**600 °F** : (Strain 2, Stress 43), (Strain 4, Stress 50), (Strain 6, Stress 53) [cite: 7, 9]
  - [cite_start]**1000 °F** : (Strain 2, Stress 41), (Strain 4, Stress 45), (Strain 6, Stress 47) [cite: 8, 10]
  - [cite_start]**1400 °F** : (Strain 2, Stress 36), (Strain 4, Stress 40), (Strain 5, Stress 40) [cite: 13]
- **Description Narrative** : Le graphique présente deux types de courbes pour l'alliage HS 188 : les courbes de contrainte-déformation compressive (montantes vers la droite) et les courbes de module tangent compressif (descendantes vers la droite). On observe une dégradation nette des propriétés mécaniques avec l'augmentation de la température de la température ambiante (RT) jusqu'à 1400 °F. Le module tangent chute brutalement après avoir atteint la limite proportionnelle de chaque courbe de température respective.

## Page 136

### [cite_start]ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Best-fit $\epsilon/N$ curve and cyclic stress-strain curve for HS 188 bar at 1600°F [ALLOY:HS 188] [cite: 212]

- [cite_start]**Identifiant du graphique** : Figure 6.4.2.1.8(c) [cite: 212]
- [cite_start]**Graphique 1 : Fatigue Life ($\epsilon/N$)** [cite: 180, 196]
  - **Axes** : Y = Strain Range ; X = Fatigue Life, Cycles.
  - **Points clés** : À $10^{3}$ cycles, Strain Range $\approx 10^{-2}$. À $10^{5}$ cycles, il descend à $\approx 3.5 \times 10^{-3}$.
- [cite_start]**Graphique 2 : Stable Cyclic Stress-Strain** [cite: 190, 197, 211]
  - **Axes** : Y = Stress, ksi ; X = Strain, Percent.
  - **Points clés** : (0.15%, 32 ksi), (0.2%, 38 ksi), (0.4%, 46 ksi), (0.5%, 48 ksi).
- **Description Narrative** : À 1600 °F, on note une chute significative de la contrainte cyclique stable (maximum ~48 ksi). La courbe de fatigue montre une transition plus douce entre les régimes de basse et haute fatigue.

MIL-HDBK-5J
[cite_start]31 January 2003 [cite: 194]
[cite_start]6-136 [cite: 213]

## Page 137

### [cite_start]Correlative Information for Figure 6.4.2.1.8(c) [ALLOY:HS 188] [cite: 215]

- [cite_start]**Product Form/Thickness**: Bar, 1.5 inch thick [cite: 216]
- [cite_start]**Thermal Mechanical Processing History**: Solution treated, water quenched (AMS 5772) [cite: 217]

### [cite_start]Mechanical Properties [ALLOY:HS 188] [cite: 218]

| [ALLOY_ID] + [CONDITION_TEMPER] | TUS (ksi)                         | TYS (ksi)                        | E (ksi)                            | Temp. (°F)                      |
| :------------------------------ | :-------------------------------- | :------------------------------- | :--------------------------------- | :------------------------------ |
| [HS 188 bar] [Solution treated] | [cite_start]120\* ksi [cite: 219] | [cite_start]55\* ksi [cite: 219] | NOT_SPECIFIED                      | [cite_start]75 °F [cite: 219]   |
| [HS 188 bar] [Solution treated] | NOT_SPECIFIED                     | NOT_SPECIFIED                    | [cite_start]22,406 ksi [cite: 219] | [cite_start]1600 °F [cite: 219] |

[cite_start]**Notes** : \* Minimum values from AMS 5772. [cite: 234]

### [cite_start]Stress-Strain Equations [ALLOY:HS 188] [cite: 220]

- [cite_start]**Cyclic (Companion Specimens)**: Proportional Limit = 36 ksi [cite: 221, 222]
- [cite_start]**Equation**: $(\Delta\sigma/2)=81.6(\Delta\epsilon_{p}/2)^{0.094}$ [cite: 223]

### Test Parameters and Fatigue Data [ALLOY:HS 188]

- [cite_start]**Specimen Details**: Uniform gage test section, 0.250 inch diameter [cite: 224, 225]
- [cite_start]**Reference**: 3.8.1.1.8 [cite: 226]
- [cite_start]**Strain Rate/Frequency**: 20 cpm [cite: 228]
- [cite_start]**Wave Form**: Triangular [cite: 228]
- [cite_start]**Temperature**: 1600 °F [cite: 228]
- [cite_start]**Atmosphere**: Air [cite: 228]
- [cite_start]**No. of Heats/Lots**: 1 [cite: 229]
- [cite_start]**Sample Size**: 16 [cite: 232]
- [cite_start]**Equivalent Strain Equation**: $\log N_{f} = 0.011 - 1.343 \log(\Delta\epsilon - 0.00283)$ [cite: 231]
- **Statistical Data**:
  - Std. [cite_start]Error of Estimate, Log(Life) = 0.116 [cite: 231]
  - [cite_start]Standard Deviation, Log(Life) = 0.582 [cite: 231]
  - [cite_start]$R^{2} = 96\%$ [cite: 231]

[cite_start]**Caution**: The equivalent strain model may provide unrealistic life predictions for strain ratios and ranges beyond those represented above. [cite: 233]

MIL-HDBK-5J
[cite_start]31 January 2003 [cite: 214]
[cite_start]6-137 [cite: 235]

## Page 138

### [cite_start]ANALYSE GRAPHIQUE : Best-fit $\epsilon/N$ curve and cyclic stress-strain curve for HS 188 bar at 1800°F [ALLOY:HS 188] [cite: 267]

- [cite_start]**Identifiant du graphique** : Figure 6.4.2.1.8(d) [cite: 267]
- [cite_start]**Graphique 1 : Fatigue Life ($\epsilon/N$)** [cite: 236, 253]
  - **Axes** : Y = Strain Range ; X = Fatigue Life, Cycles.
  - **Points clés** : À $10^{3}$ cycles, Strain Range $\approx 8 \times 10^{-3}$. À $10^{5}$ cycles, il descend à $\approx 2.5 \times 10^{-3}$.
- [cite_start]**Graphique 2 : Stable Cyclic Stress-Strain** [cite: 246, 256, 266]
  - **Axes** : Y = Stress, ksi ; X = Strain, Percent.
  - **Points clés** : (0.15%, 23 ksi), (0.2%, 28 ksi), (0.4%, 32 ksi), (0.5%, 35 ksi).
- **Description Narrative** : À 1800 °F, les capacités de résistance sont à leur minimum pour cette série de tests. La contrainte cyclique ne dépasse pas 35 ksi pour 0.5% de déformation.

MIL-HDBK-5J
[cite_start]31 January 2003 [cite: 252]

## Page 139

### [cite_start]Correlative Information for Figure 6.4.2.1.8(d) [ALLOY:HS 188] [cite: 270]

- [cite_start]**Product Form/Thickness**: Bar, 1.5 inch thick [cite: 271]
- [cite_start]**Thermal Mechanical Processing History**: Solution treated, water quenched (AMS 5772) [cite: 272]

### [cite_start]Mechanical Properties [ALLOY:HS 188] [cite: 273]

| [ALLOY_ID] + [CONDITION_TEMPER] | TUS (ksi)                         | TYS (ksi)                        | E (ksi)                            | Temp. (°F)                      |
| :------------------------------ | :-------------------------------- | :------------------------------- | :--------------------------------- | :------------------------------ |
| [HS 188 bar] [Solution treated] | [cite_start]120\* ksi [cite: 274] | [cite_start]55\* ksi [cite: 274] | NOT_SPECIFIED                      | [cite_start]75 °F [cite: 274]   |
| [HS 188 bar] [Solution treated] | NOT_SPECIFIED                     | NOT_SPECIFIED                    | [cite_start]20,353 ksi [cite: 274] | [cite_start]1800 °F [cite: 274] |

[cite_start]**Notes** : \* Minimum values from AMS 5772. [cite: 289]

### [cite_start]Stress-Strain Equations [ALLOY:HS 188] [cite: 275]

- [cite_start]**Cyclic (Companion Specimens)**: Proportional Limit = 23 ksi [cite: 276, 277]
- [cite_start]**Equation**: $(\Delta\sigma/2)=66.3(\Delta\epsilon_{p}/2)^{0.12}$ [cite: 278]

### Test Parameters and Fatigue Data [ALLOY:HS 188]

- [cite_start]**Specimen Details**: Uniform gage test section, 0.250 inch diameter [cite: 279, 280]
- [cite_start]**Reference**: 3.8.1.1.8 [cite: 281]
- [cite_start]**Strain Rate/Frequency**: 20 cpm [cite: 283]
- [cite_start]**Wave Form**: Triangular [cite: 283]
- [cite_start]**Temperature**: 1800 °F [cite: 283]
- [cite_start]**Atmosphere**: Air [cite: 283]
- [cite_start]**No. of Heats/Lots**: 1 [cite: 284]
- [cite_start]**Sample Size**: 15 [cite: 287]
- [cite_start]**Equivalent Strain Equation**: $\log N_{f} = 0.047 - 1.317 \log(\Delta\epsilon - 0.00239)$ [cite: 286]
- **Statistical Data**:
  - Std. [cite_start]Error of Estimate, Log(Life) = 0.012 [cite: 286]
  - [cite_start]Standard Deviation, Log(Life) = 0.063 [cite: 286]
  - [cite_start]$R^{2} = 96\%$ [cite: 286]

[cite_start]**Caution**: The equivalent strain model may provide unrealistic life predictions for strain ratios and ranges beyond those represented above. [cite: 288]

MIL-HDBK-5J
